For example, when asked to list ways Apple has used machine learning in its recent software and products, Giannandrea lists a variety of things before ultimately indicating that it&#8217;s harder to name things that don&#8217;t use machine learning than ones that do.</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote3\"><p>\n  There&#8217;s a whole bunch of new experiences that are powered by machine learning. And these are things like language translation, or on-device dictation, or our new features around health, like sleep and hand washing, and stuff we&#8217;ve released in the past around heart health and things like this. I think there are increasingly fewer and fewer places in iOS where we&#8217;re not using machine learning. It&#8217;s hard to find a part of the experience where you&#8217;re not doing some predictive [work].\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p4\">One interesting tidbit mentioned by both Giannandrea and Borchers is that Apple&#8217;s increased dependence on machine learning hasn&#8217;t led to the company talking about ML non-stop. I&#8217;ve noticed this too &#8211; whereas a few years ago the company might have thrown out &#8216;machine learning&#8217; countless times during a keynote presentation, these days it&#8217;s intentionally more careful and calculated in naming the term, and I think for good reason. As Giannandrea puts it, &#8220;I think that this is the future of the computing devices that we have, is that they be smart, and that, that smart sort of disappear.&#8221; Borchers expounds on that idea:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote5\"><p>\n  This is clearly our approach, with everything that we do, which is, &#8216;Let&#8217;s focus on what the benefit is, not how you got there.&#8217; And in the best cases, it becomes automagic. It disappears&#8230; and you just focus on what happened, as opposed to how it happened.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p6\">The full interview covers subjects like Apple&#8217;s Neural Engine, Apple Silicon for Macs, the benefits of handling ML tasks on-device, and much more, including a fun story from Giannandrea&#8217;s early days at Apple. 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Fortnite Developer Epic Games Sues Apple Alleging Anti-Competitive App Store and Payment Processing Behavior","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=64080","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Nineteen%20Eighty-Fortnite-00-00-03-362-1597354252638.png\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">Apple has been on <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/09/apple-goes-to-war-with-the-gaming-industry/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a rapidly accelerating collision course</a> with the videogame industry for the past couple of weeks. Not long after <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2020/07/29/apple-google-facebook-amazon-congress-hearing/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Congressional hearings investigating anti-competitive conduct</a> by large technology companies, including Apple, <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/8/6/21357771/apple-cloud-gaming-microsoft-xcloud-google-stadia-ios-app-store-guidelines-violations\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Microsoft ended the TestFlight beta of its xCloud app</a> because Apple wouldn&#8217;t approve the game streaming service. Today, the conflict came to a head when Epic Games, the maker of the hugely popular Fortnite, filed a private antitrust suit against Apple.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">In hindsight, the series of events that unfolded today appear to be part of a carefully orchestrated plan leading to the filing of the lawsuit. The day began with Epic offering in-game currency at a discount in the iOS version of the game <a href=\"https://www.epicgames.com/fortnite/en-US/news/the-fortnite-mega-drop-permanent-discounts-up-to-20-percent\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">using Epic&#8217;s own payment system</a> in clear violation of App Store guidelines. Apple responded by <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/8/13/21366438/apple-fortnite-ios-app-store-violations-epic-payments\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">pulling the game from the App Store</a>. In a statement to The Verge, <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/8/13/21366438/apple-fortnite-ios-app-store-violations-epic-payments\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Apple said</a>:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote4\"><p>\n  Today, Epic Games took the unfortunate step of violating the App Store guidelines that are applied equally to every developer and designed to keep the store safe for our users. As a result their Fortnite app has been removed from the store. Epic enabled a feature in its app which was not reviewed or approved by Apple, and they did so with the express intent of violating the App Store guidelines regarding in-app payments that apply to every developer who sells digital goods or services.</p>\n<p>  Epic has had apps on the App Store for a decade, and have benefited from the App Store ecosystem - including its tools, testing, and distribution that Apple provides to all developers. Epic agreed to the App Store terms and guidelines freely and we&#8217;re glad they&#8217;ve built such a successful business on the App Store. The fact that their business interests now lead them to push for a special arrangement does not change the fact that these guidelines create a level playing field for all developers and make the store safe for all users. We will make every effort to work with Epic to resolve these violations so they can return Fortnite to the App Store.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p5\">Shortly after the game was pulled from the App Store by Apple, Epic filed a 62-page lawsuit in the United States District Court for the Northern District of California alleging violations of the federal Sherman Act and a similar California state statute.</p>\n<p id=\"p6\"><a href=\"https://cdn2.unrealengine.com/apple-complaint-734589783.pdf\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">According to Epic</a>:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote7\"><p>\n  Apple has become what it once railed against: the behemoth seeking to control markets, block competition, and stifle innovation. Apple is bigger, more powerful, more entrenched, and more pernicious than the monopolists of yesteryear. At a market cap of nearly $2 trillion, Apple&#8217;s size and reach far exceeds that of any technology monopolist in history.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p8\">The complaint alleges anti-competitive conduct in connection with the distribution of iOS apps and in-app payment processing. According to Epic:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote9\"><p>\n  But for Apple&#8217;s illegal restraints, Epic would provide a competing app store on iOS devices, which would allow iOS users to download apps in an innovative, curated store and would provide users the choice to use Epic&#8217;s or another third-party&#8217;s in-app payment processing tool.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p10\">The lawsuit concludes with a request that the court issue an injunction prohibiting the behavior, declaring it unlawful, and ordering other equitable relief to prevent Apple&#8217;s actions and remedy the alleged harm that has been caused.</p>\n<p id=\"p11\">The lawsuit was followed by an in-game video parodying Apple&#8217;s famous 1984 commercial asking Fortnite gamers to &#8220;Join the fight to stop 2020 from becoming &#8216;1984.&#8217;&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\" id=\"div12\"><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" type=\"text/html\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/euiSHuaw6Q4?version=3&#38;rel=1&#38;fs=1&#38;autohide=2&#38;showsearch=0&#38;showinfo=1&#38;iv_load_policy=1&#38;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\"></iframe></div>\n<p id=\"p13\">Based on the timing of events, it appears that Epic intentionally violated Apple&#8217;s app review guidelines to pick a fight. I would be surprised if backroom negotiations didn&#8217;t precede the filing of the lawsuit, but regardless, Epic&#8217;s actions raise another line of attack against the way Apple runs the App Store. What&#8217;s different about Epic&#8217;s lawsuit is that it&#8217;s brought by a well-funded, private company that has hired <a href=\"https://www.cravath.com\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">one of the biggest global law firms</a> to fight for it. Barring a quick settlement, this will cost both companies a lot of money and subject Apple to bad publicity over a much longer period of time than a day&#8217;s testimony in front of Congress ever could.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Plus, it&#8217;s made in Italy.</p>\n</p><a href='https://club.macstories.net/?utm_source=ms&#038;utm_medium=rss'>Join Now</a>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 13 Aug 2020 21:34:58 +0000","feedId":526,"bgimg":"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Nineteen%20Eighty-Fortnite-00-00-03-362-1597354252638.png","linkMd5":"4ec506a90478b396686a7f1f26c7970e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn17@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-54-46-720_7416fcab14cd2a0a.webp","destWidth":1440,"destHeight":1078,"author":"John Voorhees","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Nineteen%20Eighty-Fortnite-00-00-03-362-1597354252638.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn9@2020_6/2020/08/16/11-54-46-732_7416fcab14cd2a0a.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Soor 2 Review: Magic Mixes and Release Alerts Elevate the Beautiful Apple Music Client","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63915","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\">\n <img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/d5461bb7-4b02-477d-bc4b-e0d8fdef53fc.png\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></img>\n</div> \n<p id=\"p2\">Following the debut of Apple’s <a href=\"https://developer.apple.com/musickit/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">MusicKit API</a>, which enables third parties to build apps and web experiences that directly integrate with Apple Music, 2019 was a big year for third-party Apple Music clients on the App Store. We’ve written about several of <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/reviews/marvis-review-the-ultra-customizable-apple-music-client/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">these</a> <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/reviews/miximum-smart-apple-music-playlists-on-ios/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">apps</a>, but the earliest and highest profile debut of the year was <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/soor/id1439731526?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Soor</a>, a meticulously designed client that distinguishes itself with a fully customizable Home view for displaying only the content sections you care about –&nbsp;choosing from things like Recently Added, Playlists, Recently Played, New Releases, For You, and more. Federico reviewed <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/reviews/soor-a-third-party-apple-music-client-for-iphone/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the launch version of Soor</a> and found a lot to like about its unique approach, but he ultimately was disappointed by the absence of certain functionality that’s readily available in Apple’s first-party Music app.</p> \n<p id=\"p3\">In the nearly 18 months since launch, Soor has improved in significant ways. I adore the throwback <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cover_Flow\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Cover Flow</a>-inspired playback screen, where you can smoothly swipe through a horizontal row of artwork, and time-synced lyrics are now available via a tight <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/musixmatch-lyrics-finder/id448278467?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Musixmatch</a> integration. There are still certain functions you’ll need to pop into Apple’s Music app for, sometimes due to Apple Music API limitations that Soor’s developer can do nothing about, and other times because the app simply doesn’t offer certain features yet – AirPlay 2, for example, is still unsupported. Overall though, for my uses at least, Soor covers enough core Apple Music functionality that there’s very little I need the first-party client for. The biggest absent feature on my wishlist is an iPad app, which I’m <a href=\"https://twitter.com/tanmays/status/1285812955779461120?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">glad to see is on the roadmap</a>, especially since iPadOS 14 will soon offer a much-improved first-party Music app.</p> \n<p id=\"p4\">Soor’s improvements have made it a truly compelling alternative to the first-party Music app, and today’s 2.0 update continues that trend by offering two big new features: magic mixes and release alerts. The latter is a nice addition, but the real pillar of this update is magic mixes.</p> \n<p id=\"p5\">\n <!--more--></p> \n<h2 id=\"magic-mixes\">Magic Mixes</h2> \n<p id=\"p6\">Magic mixes enable building highly customizable and dynamic mixes using a variety of Source, Filter, Sort, and Limit options. Since these mixes are dynamic, as new music is released or Apple makes changes to its editorially-curated playlists, your mixes update to reflect an ever-changing roster of matched songs.</p> \n<p id=\"p7\">To get started creating a magic mix, you can tap the new magic mix icon in the mini player, or hit Manage Sections at the bottom of the app to create a mix from there.</p> \n<div class=\"media-wrapper\">\n <img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/AB223E44-2588-4E0C-BC7F-A4B018CB6338-1595434087617.png\" alt=\"The vast array of magic mix configuration options.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">The vast array of magic mix configuration options.</p></img>\n</div> \n<p id=\"p9\">Sources for a magic mix can include content both from your Library and from the full Apple Music catalog. On the Library side, you can choose from albums, playlists, loved songs, recently added or recently played music, and more. When choosing sources from the Apple Music catalog you’ll see the full roster of For You<sup id=\"fnref-63915-1\"><a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63915#fn-63915-1\" class=\"jetpack-footnote\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">1</a></sup> suggested playlists and albums to choose from, plus all of the top playlists curated by Apple’s staff, or you can select hot or top songs, new releases, or even a custom search term. These source options make magic mixes more powerful than anything I’ve encountered in another music app, and the experience of choosing them is delightful thanks to some design polish in the selection process.</p> \n<p id=\"p10\">Once you’ve chosen sources for your magic mix, you can move on to filtering rules, which includes 15 different categories of filters spanning things like play count, date added, like state, explicit, title, artist, and much more. The whole process is intuitive as you select a filter then choose the rule for it using parameters like ‘Equals,’ ‘Not Equal To,’ ‘Contains,’ ‘Before’ or ‘After,’ and more.</p> \n<p id=\"p11\">The final two configuration points for your mix are sort and limit options. Limit simply lets you enter a number of tracks that you want to limit the mix to. Sort options, on the other hand, are plentiful, including things like last played, play count, release year, genre, duration, shuffled, and more. These can then be set in ascending or descending order.</p> \n<p id=\"p12\">All of this detailed walkthrough is necessary to explain how you can build some wild, fine-grained custom mixes in Soor. The fact that they update dynamically is just icing on the cake.</p> \n<p id=\"p13\">One of my favorite details about the magic mix feature is that it pairs so beautifully with Soor’s section-based design. Every magic mix you create is accessible as its own Home section, giving you the ability to customize the app’s layout with the music you care about most. For example, I’ve created an extremely simple mix that takes a single playlist and sorts its track order by release date, from newest to oldest. This mix meets a desire I’ve long had for this particular playlist, and now lives at the top of my Home layout.</p> \n<div class=\"media-wrapper\">\n <img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/FED2E2C2-BA00-4985-AF61-C4426651B92C-1595434090869.png\" alt=\"My simple, but valuable Discovered magic mix.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">My simple, but valuable Discovered magic mix.</p></img>\n</div> \n<p id=\"p15\">The playlist is called Discovered, and it’s where I save new singles I come across that I want to listen to later. Much of my music listening is album-oriented rather than centering on playlists, but Discovered is my most frequently listened to playlist because it’s where all singles go for me, whether they’re from artists I already love or new ones I find. I never add singles to my Library because they would clutter up my Recently Added screen, so instead I save them to this playlist and keep the ‘Add Playlist Songs’ Music toggle in iOS’ Settings app disabled, ensuring that tracks added to playlists won’t populate my Library.</p> \n<p id=\"p16\">The problem with this approach for saving new singles is that the first-party Music app offers no option for changing the way a playlist is sorted. So what ends up happening with my ever-growing Discovered playlist is that I hear the oldest songs, which live at the top of the playlist, far too often, while my most recently saved songs remain neglected and often forgotten at the bottom of the list. I could always use Music’s shuffle feature, but that still isn’t quite what I want, which is to simply reverse the order of the playlist so the newest songs play first and the oldest ones play last. With Soor’s ‘Release Year’ sort option set in descending order, a magic mix solves this problem. And I can not only access my reverse-order Discovered playlist as its own dedicated Home section in the app, but I can also quickly kick off playback via a shortcut.</p> \n<div class=\"media-wrapper\">\n <img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/3A59BBB9-25DA-4B6D-9210-2CAEE8E023B0-1595434093798.png\" alt=\"Adding a magic mix as a shortcut via Siri, then to my Home screen.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Adding a magic mix as a shortcut via Siri, then to my Home screen.</p></img>\n</div> \n<p id=\"p18\">That’s right, every magic mix you create comes with Shortcuts support. There’s an Add to Siri button at the bottom of each magic mix edit screen, so you can start playing your custom mix with a simple Siri voice command, or by running a shortcut from the Shortcuts app. Personally, I’ve created a Home screen shortcut that kicks off my Discovered magic mix, but another thing I may consider in the future is adding it to Shortcuts’ widget. Whether run from the Home screen, or a widget, or the full Shortcuts app, or even Siri, I love how easy it is to start playing magic mixes.</p> \n<h2 id=\"release-alerts\">Release Alerts</h2> \n<p id=\"p19\">I won’t go too deep into this, since it’s a feature already available elsewhere such as in Apple’s Music app and the excellent dedicated utility, <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/musicharbor-track-new-music/id1440405750?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">MusicHarbor</a>. But it’s still worth noting that Soor now offers alerts for new releases from artists you follow, and the implementation details are quite nice.</p> \n<div class=\"media-wrapper\">\n <img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/78F5B6D7-9007-4FC1-9E26-1BC538867C7C-1595434094668.png\" alt=\"Soor offers a feature-rich release alert system.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Soor offers a feature-rich release alert system.</p></img>\n</div> \n<p id=\"p21\">There’s a new bell icon in the top-right corner of Soor’s interface which you can tap to view and manage release alerts. This screen will show you all artists you currently follow, provide the option of searching for new artists to follow or choose from suggestions that are based on your playback history. The only missing option I’d want is the ability to automatically follow all artists in my Library.</p> \n<p id=\"p22\">Besides serving as a way to find artists to follow, this screen also displays all recent releases from artists you’re following, upcoming releases from those artists, and also a list of upcoming releases from all artists. It’s a full-featured release tracking experience that’s elegantly integrated into the app.</p> \n<p id=\"p23\">Soor presents new releases not only in the dedicated hub behind the bell icon, but also at the top of the app’s Home view. If there are multiple new releases, they’ll be presented in a stack that you can cycle through by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/tanmays/status/1285802405678821376?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">swiping on the displayed music artwork</a>, and there’s an X button in the top-right corner of the banner to dismiss it.</p> \n<p id=\"p24\">Soor’s release tracking feature more closely resembles the power of MusicHarbor than the minimalist approach of Apple Music, which gives it a unique edge since unlike MusicHarbor, it’s built into a full-fledged Apple Music client, mitigating the need to keep an extra utility app around.</p> \n<hr id=\"hr25\">\n <p id=\"p26\"><strong>iOS 14 Disclaimer:</strong> If you’re using the iOS 14 beta, currently there’s a bug with the Apple Music API that causes certain iOS 14 users to see a ‘Session Expired’ message when pulling new data from Apple Music, which happens upon every app launch. I haven’t had this problem myself at all, but Soor’s developer Tanmay explained to me that it only affects iOS 14 users who newly install the app, not existing users. He <a href=\"https://openradar.appspot.com/radar?id=4956912038707200\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">has a radar filed</a>, so hopefully the problem will be fixed in a new iOS 14 beta soon, but if you’re new to Soor and using iOS 14, this is a short-term annoyance you should be aware of.</p> \n <hr id=\"hr27\">\n  <p id=\"p28\">Soor’s debut last year brought a lot of design elegance and worked exactly like my ideal music app would: a single-screen interface with fully customizable sections, so that I see only the music I care about most and it’s all quickly accessible. The app did come with drawbacks though, as Federico’s initial review highlighted.</p> \n  <p id=\"p29\">With its evolution over the last 18 months, Soor has become more compelling than ever. There’s still no iPad app or AirPlay 2, and there will always be certain features exclusive to Apple’s first-party client, but if the strengths of Soor – UI customization, magic mixes, and a beautiful, top-tier design that extends from the Home view to the playback screen – are of greater value to you than its drawbacks, then the app might just become your new favorite Apple Music client.</p> \n  <p id=\"p30\">Soor is <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/soor/id1439731526?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">available on the App Store</a> as a one-time purchase.</p> \n  <div class=\"footnotes\" id=\"div31\"> \n   <hr>\n    <ol>\n     <li id=\"fn-63915-1\"> Which Apple has now rebranded Listen Now in iOS 14.&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63915#fnref-63915-1\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">↩︎</a> </li> \n    </ol>\n   </hr>\n  </div> \n  <hr />\n  <h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3>\n  <p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week; it’s also a way to support us directly.</p> <p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Plus, it’s made in Italy.</p> </p>\n  <a href=\"https://club.macstories.net/?utm_source=ms&amp;utm_medium=rss\">Join Now</a>\n </hr>\n</hr>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 22 Jul 2020 Christoffel","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/d5461bb7-4b02-477d-bc4b-e0d8fdef53fc.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn77@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-54-47-343_d2540dccb7283227.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/AB223E44-2588-4E0C-BC7F-A4B018CB6338-1595434087617.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn90@2020_1/2020/08/16/11-54-55-475_ee8a5985807ecdf7.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/FED2E2C2-BA00-4985-AF61-C4426651B92C-1595434090869.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn82@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-54-52-988_8451e1fb098ee08b.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/3A59BBB9-25DA-4B6D-9210-2CAEE8E023B0-1595434093798.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn38@2020_2/2020/08/16/11-54-48-580_445b9bfbf7b5a5e7.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/78F5B6D7-9007-4FC1-9E26-1BC538867C7C-1595434094668.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn5@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-55-01-563_843c2498d98fb566.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Mac Catalyst 2.0: Doubling Down on the Alignment of the Mac and iPad","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63957","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%204%400-1596037247109.5x.png\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">WWDC 2020 brought Mac Catalyst into sharper focus than ever before. Introduced as <a href=\"https://youtu.be/UThGcWBIMpU\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">an unnamed &#8216;sneak peek&#8217; in 2018</a>, Mac Catalyst offered the promise of a simple and efficient way for iPad developers to bring their apps to <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/apple-events/june-2019/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">100 million Mac users</a>. The reality was that it can be hard to transition an app from an iPad to a Mac, and the results weren&#8217;t always great.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">The trouble was the result of a confluence of multiple factors, including:</p>\n<ul id=\"ul4\"><li>The first iteration of Mac Catalyst used iPad design conventions in places that felt out of place on the Mac</li>\n<li>There was too little documentation</li>\n<li>Excitement surrounding SwiftUI left developers wondering whether Apple was committed to Mac Catalyst</li>\n</ul><aside class=\"aside aligncenter aside-narrow\" id=\"aside5\"><h3 class=\"pre-title\" id=\"supported-by\">Supported By</h3>\n<h2 id=\"concepts\">Concepts</h2>\n\n<p></p><center><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/icon-1595254554207.png\" alt=\"\"></center>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://concepts.app/download?utm_source=macstories)\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer noopener noreferrer\">Concepts</a></strong>: Sketch, Note, Draw</p>\n</aside><p id=\"p6\">WWDC 2020 was different. Apple introduced what was effectively Mac Catalyst 2.0 with its Optimized for Mac initiative, a separate Mac Catalyst path that follows Mac conventions more closely but requires more work. The company also built Messages and Maps, two of its flagship apps, using Mac Catalyst, demonstrating a deeper commitment to the technology than ever before. The result is a brighter future for Mac Catalyst that clearly has a role to play alongside SwiftUI and Apple&#8217;s other frameworks.</p>\n<p id=\"p7\">To understand where Mac Catalyst is heading, though, we first need to understand where it has been over the past two years.</p>\n<p id=\"p8\"><!--more--></p>\n<h2 id=\"just-check-the-box\">Just Check the Box</h2>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/2018-02-06-05-680-1596036268188.png\" alt=\"Project Sneak Peek.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Project Sneak Peek.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p10\">Mac Catalyst has had a short but unusual history. In a rare move for Apple, the company provided a sneak peek of the then-unnamed project at WWDC in 2018. At the same time, Apple also revealed that it had used an early version of Catalyst to bring Stocks, News, Voice Memos, and Home to the Mac from the iPad.</p>\n<p id=\"p11\">The reception from observers and developers was <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2018/6/7/17438450/apple-marzipan-mac-ios-apps-port-mojave-appkit-uikit-future-platform-software\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">lukewarm</a>. None of those first four Catalyst apps involved the kind of complex UIs commonly found in many Mac apps, and all of them broke longstanding Mac design conventions. That left a lot of developers and users uneasy about Catalyst&#8217;s future, but most were willing to wait to see what Apple had in store for third-party developers before judging the technology too harshly.</p>\n<p id=\"p12\">WWDC 2019 helped to a degree, but not enough. On the one hand, Apple revealed Podcasts, an imperfect but more complex and Mac-like app built with Mac Catalyst. On the other hand, though, Apple didn&#8217;t update the original four Catalyst apps, leaving observers to <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2019/10/7/20902020/macos-catalina-review-apple-music-podcasts-catalyst-ipad-apps\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">question the company&#8217;s commitment</a> to Mac Catalyst.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%207%400-1596037377768.5x.png\" alt=\"The original four Mac Catalyst apps &#8211; Stocks, News, Voice Memos, and Home &#8211; have been joined by five others.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">The original four Mac Catalyst apps &#8211; Stocks, News, Voice Memos, and Home &#8211; have been joined by five others.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p14\">Apple also <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/apple-events/june-2019/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">oversold Catalyst at WWDC 2019</a> as a simple checkbox transformation from iPad to Mac app. It turned out to be anything but that. It was certainly possible to get many apps up and running relatively quickly by checking a box in Xcode, but <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/linked/the-important-role-design-plays-in-building-a-mac-catalyst-app/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">refining those apps</a> so they fit in reasonably well on the Mac was another story altogether. Creating something that fits in with AppKit-based apps <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/linked/pcalc-developer-james-thomson-shares-his-catalyst-experience/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">took substantial work in many cases</a> due to the inherent limits of Catalyst itself.</p>\n<p id=\"p15\">When Catalina shipped in the fall, the result was a raft of new Mac Catalyst apps, <a href=\"https://daringfireball.net/2019/12/catalyst_two_months_in\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">many of which weren&#8217;t very good</a>. There were exceptions, which <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/news/macos-catalina-the-macstories-review/8/#catalyst-apps\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">I covered in my Catalina review</a> and subsequently, but with developers stuck fighting with their tools and having to recreate controls that weren&#8217;t made readily available, <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/linked/catalysts-rough-edges-risks-alienating-developers-and-users-alike/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">many were left wondering what the future held for Mac Catalyst</a>.</p>\n<p id=\"p16\">The cloud over Mac Catalyst was exacerbated by the debut of SwiftUI, Apple&#8217;s declarative system for building modern UIs using the Swift programming language. Introduced alongside Catalyst in 2019, Apple made it clear that its ultimate goal was to allow developers to use SwiftUI to build interfaces across all of its platforms. The message was clear: <a href=\"https://inessential.com/2019/06/07/the_next_era_ends_the_swift_era_begins\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">SwiftUI was the future</a>.</p>\n<p id=\"p17\">SwiftUI managed to muddy the waters to the point that John Gruber declared that Mac Catalyst had been <a href=\"https://daringfireball.net/linked/2019/06/11/simmons-swift-era\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">effectively deprecated before it left the gate</a>. With Catalyst clearly a transitional technology and SwiftUI poised to rule the future, developers were left wondering if adopting it was a gamble on a dead-end, also-ran technology. It didn&#8217;t help that <a href=\"https://tla.systems/blog/2019/10/08/catalytic-converter/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">developer documentation was sparse</a>, the original four Mac Catalyst apps sat largely untouched throughout 2019, Podcasts, though better than earlier Catalyst releases, was aided by non-public APIs, and <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/news/macos-will-soon-support-universal-apps-enabling-a-single-purchase-for-mac-iphone-and-ipad-apps/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">universal purchases couldn&#8217;t include Mac Catalyst apps</a> until earlier this year. As a result, many developers decided to <a href=\"https://www.macworld.com/article/3405122/catalyst-reveals-apples-struggle-with-the-future-of-the-mac.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">sit out the first wave of Catalyst apps</a>.</p>\n<p id=\"p18\">What WWDC 2020 confirmed was that the addition of Mac Catalyst apps to universal purchases a few months earlier was a sign of things to come. Apple was listening to developers about the pain points of developing Catalyst apps and making adjustments. The company was refining its message and providing a clearer path forward for developers.</p>\n<p id=\"p19\">In hindsight, revealing Mac Catalyst as a &#8216;sneak peek&#8217; in 2018 may have been a mistake. The desire to send a message to developers that a new era of alignment between the iPad and Mac was coming is understandable. However, without a full understanding of the implications of SwiftUI or knowledge of the upcoming design changes to Big Sur and the Apple Silicon transition, too much of the story remained a black box that left developers perplexed. It&#8217;s a good example of how little is to be gained from a secretive company like Apple revealing an isolated part of its plans for the future.</p>\n<h2 id=\"mac-catalyst-comes-into-focus\">Mac Catalyst Comes Into Focus</h2>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%208%400-1596037508714.5x.png\" alt=\"Third-party Mac Catalyst apps highlighted at WWDC 2020 during the keynote.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Third-party Mac Catalyst apps highlighted at WWDC 2020 during the keynote.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p21\">What has changed is that the paths to the future of development across all of Apple&#8217;s platforms have finally come into focus. WWDC 2020 confirmed developers&#8217; hunch that SwiftUI is the future. However, that comes with a big caveat. SwiftUI may be the future, but it&#8217;s also not entirely ready for the present. As far as SwiftUI has come in its first year, there are still limitations that mean it isn&#8217;t a workable solution for every new app, let alone the millions of existing apps.</p>\n<p id=\"p22\">SwiftUI&#8217;s future is bright, and I fully expect that we will see more new apps written with it. Still, we&#8217;re a long way from putting the final nail in Mac Catalyst&#8217;s coffin. The present is very much a hybrid world where Mac Catalyst will play a crucial transition role in making the Mac app ecosystem as vibrant as that of iOS and iPadOS and driving developers to adopt the current-generation iPadOS features that translate to Mac features.</p>\n<p id=\"p23\">Several aspects of WWDC 2020 and its immediate aftermath should give any developer who sat out the first wave of Mac Catalyst apps confidence to build an app with the technology. One is the new features that address many of the early complaints leveled against Catalyst, including:</p>\n<ul id=\"ul24\"><li>An AppKit date picker which has replaced the tumbler-style picker that&#8217;s been around since the first iPhone was released</li>\n<li>Pull-down menus</li>\n<li>Keyboard event enhancements and cursor control</li>\n<li>tvOS focus event handlers</li>\n<li>Photo extensions</li>\n<li>Better window and tab management</li>\n<li>A color picker and color well</li>\n</ul><p id=\"p25\">Apple has also finally addressed the lack of documentation with <a href=\"https://developer.apple.com/tutorials/mac-catalyst\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a terrific tutorial and other materials</a> that debuted just last week.</p>\n<p id=\"p26\">Also included in the enhancements to Mac Catalyst is a new mode that Apple calls &#8216;<a href=\"https://developer.apple.com/wwdc20/10056\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Optimized for Mac</a>,&#8217; which changes the default scaling of an iPad app from 77% to 100% and results in crisper text and graphics. Optimized for Mac also includes Mac-style controls that match macOS control sizes. These will require developers to make adjustments in many cases to ensure that the controls don&#8217;t break the layout of their apps. Buttons, pickers, sliders, and other controls are equivalent to what developers would get when building an AppKit app, and some controls like checkboxes are only available to Optimized for Mac apps. The trade-off for a Mac Catalyst app that hues more closely to traditional conventions is that building an Optimized for Mac Catalyst app requires more work than a standard Mac Catalyst app.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Screenshot%202020-06-22%2018-1592874941210.46.31.png\" alt=\"'Optimized for Mac' added many more Mac-like control options for Mac Catalyst apps.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">&#8216;Optimized for Mac&#8217; added many more Mac-like control options for Mac Catalyst apps.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p28\">Between standard Mac Catalyst apps and ones that are Optimized for Mac, the landscape Apple has covered is substantially broader than what was covered with the first iteration of Mac Catalyst. The quick and expedient way of building a Mac Catalyst app that&#8217;s scaled to 77%, so its UI elements work better, has gained meaningful improvements. Now, though, there&#8217;s an entirely different, alternative path developers can take that provides a much more Mac-like product. It&#8217;s more work to be sure, but it also demonstrates that Apple cares about more than just making it easier for developers to add iPad apps to the Mac. It&#8217;s also about giving developers the tools to make a Mac Catalyst app that&#8217;s at home on the Mac. At the same time, though, the simpler Mac Catalyst path acknowledges the practical reality that creating an Optimized for Mac version isn&#8217;t always economical.</p>\n<p id=\"p29\"><a href=\"https://developer.apple.com/wwdc20/10143\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">2020&#8217;s Mac Catalyst story</a> is a more complicated narrative than &#8216;check a box, and your iPad app becomes a Mac app,&#8217; but it&#8217;s also one that tells a more compelling story that fits with the alignment of the Mac and iPad as mutually reinforcing systems. The same thing can be seen in the redesign of macOS. The facile view is that the Mac is being remade in the iPad&#8217;s image. However, this perspective ignores the migration of features like sidebars, Finder-like file navigation, and cursor support from the Mac to the iPad. Each is evolving based on an overarching vision of creating a familiar but platform-specific UI that helps make users comfortable on any of Apple&#8217;s devices without learning different interactions and design metaphors where they don&#8217;t serve the unique qualities of each device.</p>\n<p id=\"p30\">To that end, the iPad and Mac now share idioms like the sidebar, toolbars, and app icons that vary depending on the platform but are instantly recognizable. That lowers the barrier for consumers who started on the iPad, making it easier for them to use a Mac too.</p>\n<p id=\"p31\">Apple also did a better job at WWDC 2020 of articulating Mac Catalyst&#8217;s position among the company&#8217;s many developer tools. Developers with a mature AppKit version of an app are not being encouraged to abandon AppKit. Those frameworks may not be the long-term future of Mac development, but they aren&#8217;t being deprecated any time soon. Likewise, iPadOS developers with an established UIKit app aren&#8217;t being encouraged to leave UIKit behind. Instead, iPad developers have options that range from running their app directly on Apple Silicon-based Macs with no changes to building standard Mac Catalyst apps and Optimized for Mac apps. It&#8217;s a practical, realistic acknowledgment that the economics of moving an app from the iPad to the Mac vary widely, so the development paths should too.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/apple_macos-bigsur_maps-curatedguides_06222020-1592874779715.jpg\" alt=\"Maps and Messages are both Mac Catalyst apps in macOS 11 Big Sur.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Maps and Messages are both Mac Catalyst apps in macOS 11 Big Sur.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p33\">However, of all the announcements at WWDC this year, the one that should give developers and users the most confidence that Apple is committed to Mac Catalyst is that it rebuilt Messages and Maps with Mac Catalyst. Both apps are central to the iPhone and iPad experience but had fallen behind on the Mac. Even in the early betas of Big Sur, Messages and Maps are solid, faithful Mac versions of their iPad counterparts. They are also substantially deeper, feature-rich apps than the early Mac Catalyst apps Apple released.</p>\n<hr id=\"hr34\"><p id=\"p35\">A catalyst increases the rate of change in a chemical reaction. In retrospect, it&#8217;s an aptly descriptive name for Mac Catalyst. Apple has been experimenting with ways to jump-start the Mac app market for years. The Mac App Store and <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/news/apple-redesigns-mac-app-store-with-ios-like-editorial-focus-new-product-pages-and-more/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">its subsequent redesign</a> didn&#8217;t seem to move the needle substantially, but I remain optimistic that Mac Catalyst will do so <a href=\"https://www.macworld.com/article/1151235/apple-rolls.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">with time</a>. Ultimately SwiftUI, which is rapidly developing on a parallel path, will likely eclipse Catalyst, but that reality is still years away because of millions of UIKit apps already on the market. Rewriting those apps for AppKit makes no sense for many developers, as demonstrated by the lack of iPad apps that have made their way to the Mac already. SwiftUI isn&#8217;t a realistic alternative for most of those apps, either.</p>\n<p id=\"p36\">With Mac Catalyst, there&#8217;s an opportunity for developers to significantly increase the potential size of the market for their apps without taking much risk. Some of those new Mac Catalyst apps will be subpar, just like there are junky iPhone and iPad apps. I&#8217;m not a fan of lousy apps, but I&#8217;m still glad that the barrier to entry to the App Store is low. It opens opportunities for newcomers who might otherwise find it too hard to get started.</p>\n<p id=\"p37\">I expect Mac Catalyst will have the same effect. More developers than ever before have access to the Mac App Store. That will create competition that pushes all developers to make better products for their users, regardless of the underlying technology used to build it. In my book, that is how it should be and the best way to strengthen the Mac as a platform.</p>\n<hr id=\"hr38\"><p id=\"p39\"><em>You can also follow our 2020 Summer OS Preview Series through our <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/tag/os-preview-2020/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">dedicated hub</a>, or <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/tag/os-preview-2020/feed/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">subscribe to its RSS feed</a>.</em></p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Plus, it&#8217;s made in Italy.</p>\n</p><a href='https://club.macstories.net/?utm_source=ms&#038;utm_medium=rss'>Join Now</a>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 29 Jul 2020 16:12:04 +0000","feedId":526,"bgimg":"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%204%400-1596037247109.5x.png","linkMd5":"ebbdcaaa189992c05ede597eb2629669","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn31@2020_5/2020/08/16/11-54-46-520_a18fc1bd3e031a4e.webp","destWidth":2880,"destHeight":1620,"author":"John Voorhees","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%204%400-1596037247109.5x.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn61@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-54-54-105_a18fc1bd3e031a4e.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/icon-1595254554207.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn77@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-54-48-556_e03c46ffe05a8718.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/2018-02-06-05-680-1596036268188.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn21@2020_1/2020/08/16/11-54-47-690_f576c8ab86fd6a19.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%207%400-1596037377768.5x.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn13@2020_2/2020/08/16/11-54-50-825_52882bc29736faa8.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%208%400-1596037508714.5x.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn25@2020_1/2020/08/16/11-54-48-481_1570376f4946fba4.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Screenshot%202020-06-22%2018-1592874941210.46.31.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn53@2020_6/2020/08/16/11-54-51-354_2c2e52a14638b7f9.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/apple_macos-bigsur_maps-curatedguides_06222020-1592874779715.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn5@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-54-50-950_171f413641acc278.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Game Day: Good Sudoku","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63912","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/C72F8C4A-AC9D-4346-B69B-4339241A25A6-1595422990123.png\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">Zach Gage has a knack for giving classic games an interesting twist. Sometimes that means turning the rules upside down and inside out like <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/flipflop-solitaire/id1256860418\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Flipflop Solitaire</a> or <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/really-bad-chess/id1109751921\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Really Bad Chess</a>. Other times, it means removing the tedious and boring parts of games to breathe new life into them, which is precisely what he and Jack Schlesinger have accomplished with <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id1489118195\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Good Sudoku</a>.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">I started with Good Sudoku as a novice. I&#8217;ve played sudoku before and knew the rules, but it&#8217;s not a game that has ever grabbed me and stuck. As a result, as much as I&#8217;ve enjoyed Gage&#8217;s other games, I approached Good Sudoku with a healthy dose of skepticism. However, after several days of playing the game, I&#8217;ve found that stripped of its tedious aspects, sudoku is engaging to the point of being addicting and a whole lot of fun.</p>\n<p id=\"p4\"><!--more--></p>\n<p id=\"p5\">If you haven&#8217;t played sudoku before, the basics are pretty simple. It&#8217;s played on a 9 x 9 grid subdivided into smaller 3 x 3 grids. The object is to fill the grid with the digits 1 - 9, so there&#8217;s only one of each numeral in a row of 9 squares, a column of 9 squares, and the 3 x 3 sub-grids called houses.</p>\n<p id=\"p6\">Each board is filled in with some numbers to start, and the rest of the squares are left blank for you to fill in, which is where things get tricky. As Gage and Schlesinger explain on the game&#8217;s website, sudoku puzzles are generated programmatically, allowing puzzle creators to dial in their difficulty. Gage and Schlesinger built a sudoku generator that created the over 70,000 puzzles in the game, but they didn&#8217;t stop there. Instead, they chose to run the puzzle generation AI in the background as you play, allowing the game to offer insights, tools that improve the experience, and hints, all of which remove the most frustrating aspects of the game.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/B848107D-EF4C-4E59-85E2-A3F3A78FFA51-1595420297258.png\" alt=\"Good Sudoku uses a dedicated number pad and a system to show you your options.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Good Sudoku uses a dedicated number pad and a system to show you your options.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p8\">Good Sudoku uses a dedicated onscreen number pad for filling out puzzles, a note-taking system, and hints to help you learn increasingly sophisticated techniques for solving puzzles. By default, tapping on a number in the number pad highlights every instance of that number in the puzzle and the other squares affected by it, leaving only the open spots for the number unmarked. However, this can be turned off or adjusted in settings.</p>\n<p id=\"p9\">Also, tapping on a blank square in the puzzle displays just those digits of the number pad that can be played in that square. The combination of tools is powerful and feels a little like cheating. Still, even if you begin playing with a simple trial and error approach as I did, the assistance that Good Sudoku&#8217;s tools provide allows patterns to begin to emerge even for beginners. Instead of feeling like work, where my job is to check and recheck which numbers are still available in each column, row, and house, I found myself exploring the relationship between the way the numbers were laid out on the grid and considering strategies for solving them.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/B884778D-2BB9-423E-A4C1-B28B641AC822-1595420055707.png\" alt=\"Good Sudoku&#8217;s focus mode and its note-taking system make it easy to keep track of possible solutions.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Good Sudoku&#8217;s focus mode and its note-taking system make it easy to keep track of possible solutions.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p11\">Good Sudoku includes a note-taking system too. You can display all the numbers that can be played for an individual square or all squares. Also, Accent Notes and Cross-Out Notes can be used to eliminate specific numbers from consideration or to assure you that a number goes in one of a couple of squares.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/96AC5B95-61FC-4127-8FB3-B42B28F25C71-1595419484413.png\" alt=\"Good Sudoku includes multiple levels of difficulty, resources for learning new puzzle-solving strategies, and daily challenges with leaderboards.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Good Sudoku includes multiple levels of difficulty, resources for learning new puzzle-solving strategies, and daily challenges with leaderboards.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p13\">If you back yourself into an unsolvable corner, Good Sudoku lets you know and can rewind your moves to the first spot where the puzzle can still be solved. There&#8217;s also an introduction to the basics of how to solve puzzles, help tips throughout, and an entire section called Improve that&#8217;s dedicated to demonstrating strategies for solving puzzles. Coupled with puzzles divided across multiple levels of difficulty and modes, three daily challenges that get harder throughout the week, and global leaderboards, Good Sudoku is a rich, deep puzzle game that will grow with you as your skills develop, keeping the game fun and challenging</p>\n<p id=\"p14\">I&#8217;m a big fan of Good Sudoku&#8217;s design too. It shares a similar aesthetic to previous releases by Gage that combine a focused and clear look with excellent sound design, music, and haptic feedback on the iPhone, all of which create a welcoming environment for concentrating on each puzzle.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\" id=\"div15\"><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" type=\"text/html\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/cjG9_PI5S-8?version=3&#38;rel=1&#38;fs=1&#38;autohide=2&#38;showsearch=0&#38;showinfo=1&#38;iv_load_policy=1&#38;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\"></iframe></div>\n<p id=\"p16\">Sudoku puzzles can be incredibly challenging, which is a big part of why they are fun and so popular. The downside, though, is the tedium. It&#8217;s a barrier to newcomers getting started and a layer that masks the satisfaction of seeing the deeper strategies that can be employed to solve a difficult puzzle.</p>\n<p id=\"p17\">Good Sudoku removes barriers to enjoying sudoku with excellent design. It&#8217;s not just that it looks good. It does, but Good Sudoku accomplishes something that you don&#8217;t see too often. It takes an established game and makes it better by applying computing power so that it doesn&#8217;t get in the way of enjoying the game. Whether or not you&#8217;re a fan of sudoku, an experienced player or a novice, Good Sudoku is a fresh take on a classic game that is worth checking out.</p>\n<p id=\"p18\">Good Sudoku <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id1489118195\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">can be downloaded for free from the App Store</a>. Some features are available only as part of the game&#8217;s $3.99 In-App Purchase.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. +0000","feedId":526,"bgimg":"https://56243e3f6f46fe44a301-deabeb5f3878e3553d0b065ea974f9bf.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/256px.png","linkMd5":"8ae98b211e10c8348a0bfb7e134151a3","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn89@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-54-46-345_901ee973c59d45b7.webp","destWidth":256,"destHeight":256,"author":"John Voorhees","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-itunes-2x1495584446433.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn29@2020_6/2020/08/16/11-54-48-951_44f6e726042a0d5b.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-overcast-2x1495584446439.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_1/2020/08/16/11-54-46-435_63962739202511e1.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-pocket-casts-2x1495584446442.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn74@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-54-49-676_683cc37726177cc0.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-rss-2x1495584446444.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn37@2020_5/2020/08/16/11-54-49-107_962140602f5518bd.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"GameTrack Review: An Elegant Way to Discover, Track, and Share Videogames","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=64020","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/34861865-80C3-4B32-BB36-FDA27D34199D-1596765554113-1596816625773.png\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">There is far more media I&#8217;d like to try than I have time for. Between TV shows, movies, music, books and other reading, podcasts, and videogames, the supply of content far outstrips the time I have by an order of magnitude. As a result, I&#8217;m both picky and often slow to getting around to some media, especially games, which often require a substantial time commitment. The trouble is that it&#8217;s easy to lose track of games I&#8217;ve read about, that someone has recommended, and even those that I&#8217;m in the middle of playing if I can&#8217;t play regularly.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">I&#8217;ve approached the problem in a lot of different ways. Text notes are a quick and portable solution but lack detail. Apps designed to track lots of different kinds of media have the benefit of consolidating everything in one place, but often don&#8217;t accommodate features specific to one kind of media. As a result, I&#8217;ve recently gravitated to apps that focus on just a single type of media. For videogames, that solution has been <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/gametrack/id1136800740\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">GameTrack</a>, an app that we&#8217;ve covered in our <a href=\"https://club.macstories.net\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Club MacStories</a> newsletters in the past.</p>\n<p id=\"p4\"><!--more--></p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/231C5250-34E5-40AA-AEA1-73AE47E8C62E-1596795907551-1596816726626.png\" alt=\"GameTrack&#8217;s Backlog, Archive, Wish List, and Ranked lists.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">GameTrack&#8217;s Backlog, Archive, Wish List, and Ranked lists.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p6\">The app&#8217;s tab bar is divided into four sections: Lists, Discover, Activity, and Statistics. GameTrack comes with three default lists: Backlog, Archive, and Wish List. If you subscribe you can add more lists, including ranked lists which are a fun way to pick your favorite games for a system, genre, or franchise. Backlog can be further divided into Now Playing, Play Next, and Collection, and Archive into Finished, Completed, and Abandoned. Wish List is organized by release date and can send you notifications when the games listed there become available. You can pick the platform you&#8217;re playing on when more than one is available, and games on your lists can be sorted and grouped based on multiple criteria too.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/9400BCF7-FAC3-4D7D-A23E-99EB22D1033D-1596796253404%202-1596817161692.png\" alt=\"Each game&#8217;s entry includes details drawn from the IGDB database and rich artwork.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Each game&#8217;s entry includes details drawn from the IGDB database and rich artwork.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p8\">Each game in a list includes a summary of it pulled from the IGDB database, screenshots, trailers, ratings, release date, genre, critic rating, and other metadata. GameTrack lets you move items between lists and customize entries with alternate artwork from a game&#8217;s detail view. You can also specify a completion percentage and take notes, which is a handy way to save a URL of a game&#8217;s review, leave reminders to yourself about what you want to do next in a game, or remember who recommended it. Editable metadata is also accessible from a context menu when you long-press on a game&#8217;s artwork. I only wish that URLs saved in notes were links that would open in Safari View Controller so I could view them easily in-app.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/FA5300DD-2994-42E6-ADB6-5F76C79078C0-1596796516400-1596817287430.png\" alt=\"The Discover tab is a terrific way to browse games.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">The Discover tab is a terrific way to browse games.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p10\">The Discover tab allows you to browse games in the IGDB database in categories like Featured, Popular, Upcoming, Recent, Hyped, and Just Added, as well as by platform and a handful of popular franchises. You can also search for games that you want to add to your lists from this tab.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/C7F88E3B-362C-44E5-ADB6-BCC7009B230F-1596797001359-1596817395326.png\" alt=\"Activity includes games you and the people you follow have added to GameTrack.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Activity includes games you and the people you follow have added to GameTrack.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p12\">The Activity tab serves as a reverse chronological log of games you&#8217;ve added and to which lists. Here, you&#8217;ll also find entries of anyone you follow. The feature is powered by Sign In with Apple and syncs across devices. I haven&#8217;t spent a lot of time with the Follow feature, but account activity along with lists syncs quickly and reliably and it&#8217;s easy to find and follow someone if you know what their username is, or if they share a link to their profile with you. It would be nice to discover users you don&#8217;t know that have similar tastes in games, but that isn&#8217;t currently possible.</p>\n<p id=\"p13\">Despite the discovery limitations, I like the Activity feed a lot because it provides an opportunity to connect with other users to share the games you love. The app also allows you to share individual games using the share sheet, but I&#8217;d like to share full lists of games with friends and collaborate on lists too.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/3C4FC41E-45E9-44B0-AC1D-DDA50561DC23-1596797283127-2-1596817800383.png\" alt=\"From the Account tab, you can share your profile, view recent activity, and browse statistics about your games.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">From the Account tab, you can share your profile, view recent activity, and browse statistics about your games.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p15\">The final tab is a combination Account and statistics view. From here, you can view followers and who you follow, access settings, and view and share or delete posts in your activity feed. You can also see statistics about the games in your lists broken down by categories like genre, platform, personal ratings, and your history of archiving games. Finally, you can log into your PlayStation, Xbox, and Steam accounts to track information from them as well.</p>\n<p id=\"p16\">Settings are worth mentioning, too, because GameTrack is highly customizable if you are a subscriber. You can change the app&#8217;s theme, layout, tint color, and app icon, personalizing it to suit your tastes. I particularly like the new default icon and alternative icons, which have added depth and a touch of realism to the icon&#8217;s D-pad. Of course, the original version is available too, in multiple colors and special variants. Settings is also where you can manage the details of your GameTrack account, connect your Xbox, PlayStation, and Steam accounts, and export your library data.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/4917B2DF-E3B1-4CC0-91C8-D85D8A63971C-1596797572286-1596817596854.png\" alt=\"GameTrack on the iPad.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">GameTrack on the iPad.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p18\">I&#8217;ve primarily used GameTrack on my iPhone, where the colorful game art tiles and slide-up card interface work especially well for navigating lists and searching for games. The tab bar design doesn&#8217;t translate as well to the iPad, where it is split across three columns. If my iPad is connected to a keyboard, the keyboard row often covers up GameTrack&#8217;s tab bar. I can hide the keyboard row, but it still makes navigating GameTrack too difficult. Also, as you switch tabs, the content in the second and third tabs don&#8217;t update until you select something new, which can lead to confusing or irrelevant information being displayed in them. On the iPad, GameTrack would probably benefit from considering the new sidebar layout offered with iPadOS 14, which is something developer Joe Kimberlin-Wyer has said <a href=\"https://twitter.com/joekw/status/1281308221806981121?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">he is working on</a>.</p>\n<hr id=\"hr19\"><p id=\"p20\">Despite a somewhat awkward iPad design and some wishes here and there, I love GameTrack. Now, when someone recommends a game, I quickly drop it into my Wish List for the next time I&#8217;m in the mood for a new game and have the time to play it. That&#8217;s a much better system than buying a game on a whim and letting it sit for months before I try it for the first time.</p>\n<p id=\"p21\">I&#8217;ve also found myself browsing the Discover tab a lot, too, especially when I get behind on the videogame news that I usually follow. It&#8217;s a quick way to get a fix of the latest popular games and watch a few trailers, which open in Safari View Controller so I don&#8217;t have to leave the app.</p>\n<p id=\"p22\">Videogames have been one of my outlets as I&#8217;ve spent more time at home during the global pandemic. They&#8217;ve served an important entertainment role, allowing me to escape from the constant barrage of bad news for a little while. GameTrack has reduced the friction of starting a new game, even if I&#8217;ve been away from gaming for a while, by always having something ready on one of my lists, which I love. If you&#8217;ve been looking for a way to organize your gaming life, you can&#8217;t go wrong with GameTrack.</p>\n<p id=\"p23\">GameTrack <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/gametrack/id1136800740\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">is available on the App Store</a> as a free download. Custom icons and lists, ranked lists, tints, themes, layouts, and automatically updating release dates for games are all part of a $0.99/month or $7.99/year subscription.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Voorhees","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-itunes-2x1495584446433.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn29@2020_6/2020/08/16/11-54-48-951_44f6e726042a0d5b.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-overcast-2x1495584446439.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_1/2020/08/16/11-54-46-435_63962739202511e1.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-pocket-casts-2x1495584446442.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn74@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-54-49-676_683cc37726177cc0.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-rss-2x1495584446444.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn37@2020_5/2020/08/16/11-54-49-107_962140602f5518bd.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Fiery Feeds Adds Full-Text Search, Saved Searches, iPad Pointer Support, and More","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63973","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/66caff79-2ca3-4dd1-a463-697d730d7070.png\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">When I imagine the quintessential RSS user, I think of someone who wants full control of their web reading experience. They don&#8217;t want to leave news curation up to an algorithmic service like Apple News, or a social media platform like Twitter or Facebook. They also care about tools like filtering controls, and tweaking the reading experience to their preferences. For such a user, <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/fiery-feeds-rss-reader/id1158763303?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Fiery Feeds</a> may be a natural choice due to its abundance of supported RSS services and settings to tweak, along with some key pro features. Today, Fiery Feeds is better prepared to meet the needs of that kind of user thanks to a pair of important additions: full-text search and saved searches. Throw in optimized iPad pointer support, plus a new native article rendering option, and the latest Fiery Feeds update is a compelling one.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\"><!--more--></p>\n<h2 id=\"search-improvements\">Search Improvements</h2>\n<p id=\"p4\">Saved searches are a feature commonly found in Mac apps but rarely their iOS and iPadOS counterparts. Fortunately, Fiery Feeds is the latest exception to this trend, debuting a new saved search option that&#8217;s available even on mobile-first platforms. Saved searches can be created with a simple tap on the plus button that appears any time a search is initiated, and they appear in your feed list in a dedicated section.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/31711bf7-72ce-4a91-b135-595e47b70cba.png\" alt=\"Creating a saved search.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Creating a saved search.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p6\">Saved searches would be pretty pointless were it not for another key addition to this release: full-text search. You can now enter any search term to have Fiery Feeds scan not only the title but also the body of every link in your feeds, surfacing matching articles from the flood of all your subscriptions. Full-text search and the ability to save searches seem like features designed with my &#8220;quintessential RSS user&#8221; in mind: they provide even more nuanced content controls than ever before, so you can spend your time viewing exactly the content you want.</p>\n<h2 id=\"ipad-pointer-support\">iPad Pointer Support</h2>\n<p id=\"p7\">On the iPad, today&#8217;s update brings full support for iPadOS&#8217; pointer. When you have a trackpad or mouse connected to your iPad, the pointer will adapt to different interface elements in Fiery Feeds. It will snap to buttons so you can click them more easily, morph into a text input line in search boxes, let you right-click items in your feed list or article list to open context menus, and the pointer will even highlight feeds or articles it&#8217;s hovering over. Most of this is standard protocol for pointer-optimized iPad apps, with the sole exception of the hovering behavior.</p>\n<p id=\"p8\">When I first started using the iPad&#8217;s pointer in iPadOS 13.4, I occasionally found that certain interface elements I&#8217;d expected to react with a highlighting or dimming effect when I hovered over them offered no such response; notes in a note list, for example, or folders in a folder list. Apple set the standard for this behavior and third-party apps have mostly followed suit. Fiery Feeds does things differently, however, causing cells in your feed list and article list to change color shades in response to the pointer&#8217;s presence. While it&#8217;s been interesting seeing an implementation that more closely models what I originally expected, the app has confirmed for me that I think Apple made the right call in limiting the pointer&#8217;s visual activity. I&#8217;ve found the extra visual cue more distracting than helpful in use, and wish there was an option to disable it. Ultimately though, I think it&#8217;s a matter of personal taste, and some users may find Fiery Feeds&#8217; approach exactly what they&#8217;ve been looking for from the iPad&#8217;s pointer.</p>\n<h2 id=\"miscellany\">Miscellany</h2>\n<p id=\"p9\"><strong>Native article rendering.</strong> Fiery Feeds&#8217; developer Lukas Burgstaller has built a native rendering system that parses a site&#8217;s HTML itself and uses native OS elements like UIImages and UILabels to display an article&#8217;s content. I prefer viewing articles with their source site&#8217;s design retained, so this doesn&#8217;t impact me personally, but for those who prefer the app&#8217;s uniform layout for articles&#8217; content, this change should result in improved performance.</p>\n<p id=\"p10\"><strong>Search in settings.</strong> One of my favorite details about Fiery Feeds is how customizable it is. This means the app, by necessity, has a big and complex settings screen, and before now it was easy to get a little lost in there. Now, there&#8217;s a search box in settings to help you quickly find the function you&#8217;re looking to tweak.</p>\n<hr id=\"hr11\"><p id=\"p12\">None of today&#8217;s changes to Fiery Feeds are revolutionary, but they do make the app tangibly better in key ways. Full-text search and saved searches can be extremely valuable tools, especially for users who subscribe to a lot of feeds. I&#8217;ve praised the app before for its three-column layout on iPad, so it&#8217;s great to see pointer support keep that iPad app current with modern technologies. And the miscellaneous improvements, including a fundamental change in how articles are rendered, are welcome too.</p>\n<p id=\"p13\">Fiery Feeds is available <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/fiery-feeds-rss-reader/id1158763303?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">on the App Store</a> as a free download, with an optional Premium subscription to unlock advanced features such as the new saved searches and full-text search.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Pro","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=64002","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Apple_imac-macos-photos-days-darkmode_08042020-1596553417210.jpg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">Today, Apple revealed an update to the 27-inch 5K Retina iMac with faster processors, updated graphics, more storage, and new display features. Although the new 27-inch iMac&#8217;s design is identical to the existing model, this is still a significant update compared to the iMac it replaces.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">According to <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2020/08/27-inch-imac-gets-a-major-update/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Apple&#8217;s press release</a>:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote4\"><p>\n  &#8220;Now more than ever, our customers are relying on the Mac. And many of them need the most powerful and capable iMac we&#8217;ve ever made,&#8221; said Tom Boger, Apple&#8217;s senior director of Mac and iPad Product Marketing. &#8220;With blazing performance, double the memory, SSDs across the line with quadruple the storage, an even more stunning Retina 5K display, a better camera, higher fidelity speakers, and studio-quality mics, the 27-inch iMac is loaded with new features at the same price. It&#8217;s the ultimate desktop, to work, create, and communicate.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p5\">Last updated in March 2019, the new iMac features 6 and 8-core 10th generation Intel CPUs that can reach speeds of up to 5.0GHz with Turbo Boost. Storage is all SSD now with transfer speeds up to 3.4GB/s when launching apps and large files. There&#8217;s also an 8TB SSD option for the first time, which is four times the storage available in the previous model. Until today, the standard configurations of the 27-inch iMac came with Fusion drives.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://bddf794624247cea6a0b-b4761d2ba0154d0278c36dbf2b3c114d.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/imac.jpg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p7\">The new iMac has been upgraded to AMD Radeon Pro Series 5000 graphics. The display of the iMac is the same resolution as before, but now, it comes with a new nano-texture option first seen in the Pro Display XDR, which provides a low-reflection, matte finish, and it supports Apple&#8217;s True Tone technology. The new all-in-one desktop also includes a T2 chip for boot and data security, a 1080p FaceTime HD camera, and improved speakers and microphones.</p>\n<p id=\"p8\">Apple&#8217;s other iMacs received smaller updates today too. SSDs are now standard in the 21.5-inch model, although a Fusion Drive is still an option. Also, a 10-core Intel Xeon processor is now standard in the iMac Pro.</p>\n<p id=\"p9\">Today&#8217;s updates are in line with Apple&#8217;s statements during WWDC that the company had additional updates to Macs based on Intel CPUs in the pipeline. Although Macs with ARM processors are on the way later this year, Apple has not revealed which models will be converted to ARM first. Consequently, if you need a new desktop Mac, it&#8217;s still worth considering the Intel-based models, especially the new 27-inch iMac, which is substantially improved over its last iteration.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac.
