class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">There was no better time than 2020 for my discovery of <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/portal-focus-sleep-escape/id1436994560?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Portal</a>, the immersive ambient noise app I <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/reviews/portal-review-immersive-ambient-noise-with-philips-hue-integration/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">reviewed at the start of the year</a>.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">Back in January Portal impressed me with its multifaceted approach to providing an escape from your current surroundings. Not only are the app&#8217;s 3D soundscapes of a high sound quality and perfectly paired with headphones, especially noise-cancelling ones like AirPods Pro, but Portal also engages your other senses to help you focus, sleep, or mentally escape when you can&#8217;t physically escape. One way the app does this is through its visual scenes, which provide each different sound portal with a location&#8217;s snapshot that your imagination can lock on to. Another way is via Philips Hue integration, which enables your home lights to automatically sync to different colors and brightness settings that fit best with the portal environment you&#8217;ve chosen. This combination of immersive sound with visual scenes and real-world correlation via smart lights makes Portal a uniquely holistic experience.</p>\n<p id=\"p4\">I&#8217;ve been using Portal ever since January, but even more since March, when my ability to physically leave home was drastically scaled back. I don&#8217;t use it when sleeping, but it&#8217;s certainly helped me both focus and escape, providing the much-needed feeling of being in a new environment even when my physical surroundings are left unchanged. For these reasons, as well as the presence of features like breathing exercises in the app, I find it appropriate to call Portal not just an ambient noise utility, but a wellness app too.</p>\n<p id=\"p5\">Today, Portal is launching a big 3.0 update that leans into its core strengths by providing more of what makes the app great: its portals. Previously the app offered a total of 19 portals, and today that number more than doubles as 25 new portals have been added for a total of 44 &#8211; and more are on the way.</p>\n<p id=\"p6\"><!--more--></p>\n<p id=\"p7\">With any other ambient noise app, a large batch of new sounds would be a nice addition, but not necessarily worth writing a new article about. But with Portal, since each of the 25 additions represents a real location that&#8217;s been captured and optimized for the app, and paired with a custom Hue preset, adding 25 portals was clearly a huge undertaking. That level of effort shines through with all of the app&#8217;s portals.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/01f7ebe4-a6a7-4506-a79e-2e47401147ea.png\" alt=\"A few of the new portals in version 3.0.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">A few of the new portals in version 3.0.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p9\">The set of 25 new portals is split into two collections: 14 portals from the Scottish Highlands, which were captured at wintertime, and 11 from the Slovenian Alps in summer. The app&#8217;s new content library says that a Devon &#38; Cornwall collection will be added soon too.</p>\n<p id=\"p10\">Speaking of the content library, the huge expansion of portals offered necessitated a change in how you navigate the app. Previously, all available portals resided in a simple horizontal row you could swipe through. Even with the 19 previous portals, though, this was a bit unwieldy to navigate. Now you start with a limited selection of portals, and browse new ones to add from the content library. There&#8217;s even editorial content that&#8217;s been added as you browse, so you can not only see what the location looks like and hear what it sounds like, but also read some additional context about it.</p>\n<p id=\"p11\">I&#8217;ve yet to come across a portal I didn&#8217;t enjoy, but it&#8217;s nice that you can now keep only the portals you value most. Another positive change is that all your saved portals can be rearranged in the order you prefer, making the navigation system of swiping between portals function better than before.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/9c871268-e75c-4345-aece-cdb8c7e29b74.png\" alt=\"Adding a portal to your collection.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Adding a portal to your collection.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p13\">Along with the big portal expansion and plans for continued new collections being added, Portal is introducing a membership plan today. You can still download the app for free and enjoy six portals perpetually at no cost; gaining access to the full content library, however, will require a $29.99 annual subscription for new users following a 7-day free trial. Membership revenue is intended to fuel continued creation of new portals as well as enable the app to expand beyond the iPhone and iPad &#8211; Mac and Apple TV versions are in the plans for Portal&#8217;s team. I hope support for iPad multitasking is on the roadmap too.</p>\n<p id=\"p14\">As part of this membership rollout, Portal&#8217;s developers are providing some of the most generous transition offers I&#8217;ve seen for existing users of the app. If you&#8217;ve previously paid for Portal in any way, either through unlocking the app&#8217;s In-App Purchase or buying it when it was a paid app, you&#8217;ll receive a lifetime membership entirely free. And if you&#8217;ve previously downloaded the app at all, even though you&#8217;ve never paid for it, you can unlock a lifetime membership for a one-time In-App Purchase of $9.99.</p>\n<hr id=\"hr15\"><p id=\"p16\">Portal has proven essential to my peace of mind and productivity this year as I&#8217;ve spent most of my time in a small New York City apartment, trying to work while my wife does the same just a few feet away. Combined with my AirPods Pro and noise cancellation, the app has been a dependable escape and focus tool. Both for work and relaxation, it&#8217;s hard to beat the uniquely immersive experience Portal provides. If you ever find yourself in situations &#8211; whether at home, at the office, or elsewhere &#8211; when you need to create the feeling of being transported elsewhere, but can&#8217;t actually leave, I can&#8217;t recommend Portal highly enough.</p>\n<p id=\"p17\">Portal is <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/portal-focus-sleep-escape/id1436994560?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">available on the App Store</a> for iPhone and iPad.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Plus, it&#8217;s made in Italy.</p>\n</p><a href='https://club.macstories.net/?utm_source=ms&#038;utm_medium=rss'>Join Now</a>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 13 Aug 2020 14:40:18 +0000","feedId":526,"bgimg":"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/0008f83a-2472-4658-9b51-e0784edd965d.jpeg","linkMd5":"8c0d045e2494ca319d88a42c3d0b1569","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn13@2020_5/2020/08/16/11-54-46-819_db5c4c8667427d79.webp","destWidth":3840,"destHeight":2160,"author":"Ryan Christoffel","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/0008f83a-2472-4658-9b51-e0784edd965d.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn53@2020_6/2020/08/16/11-54-49-685_db5c4c8667427d79.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/01f7ebe4-a6a7-4506-a79e-2e47401147ea.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn65@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-54-51-550_f5b36480d76d0d18.webp","https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/9c871268-e75c-4345-aece-cdb8c7e29b74.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn69@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-54-48-713_f62017a72e8ac6db.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Apple Q3 2020 Results - $59.7 Billion Revenue","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63970","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/apple_nso-bangkok_ratchaprasong_07282020-1596066012321.jpg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">Apple has just published its financial results for Q3&#160;2020. The company posted revenue of $59.7 billion.&#160;<a href=\"https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2020/07/apple-reports-third-quarter-results/?1596141043\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Apple CEO Tim Cook said</a>:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote3\"><p>\n  &#8220;Apple&#8217;s record June quarter was driven by double-digit growth in both Products and Services and growth in each of our geographic segments,&#8221; said Tim Cook, Apple&#8217;s CEO. &#8220;In uncertain times, this performance is a testament to the important role our products play in our customers&#8217; lives and to Apple&#8217;s relentless innovation. This is a challenging moment for our communities, and, from Apple&#8217;s new $100 million Racial Equity and Justice Initiative to a new commitment to be carbon neutral by 2030, we&#8217;re living the principle that what we make and do should create opportunity and leave the world better than we found it.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2 id=\"estimates-and-expectations-for-q3-2020-and-the-year-ago-quarter-q3-2019\">Estimates and Expectations for Q3&#160;2020 and the Year-Ago Quarter (Q3&#160;2019)</h2>\n<p id=\"p4\">Due to the uncertainty caused by the global pandemic, Apple did not provide financial guidance for Q3&#160;2020 during its last earnings call.</p>\n<p id=\"p5\">Going into today&#8217;s call,&#160;<a href=\"https://finance.yahoo.com/news/analysts-look-to-hints-of-i-phone-12-delays-in-apples-q-3-2020-earnings-report-151355516.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Yahoo Finance said that</a>:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote6\"><p>\n  Much of the earnings focus, however, will be on whether Cook and company will provide guidance for fiscal Q4, which could offer a hint about any potential delays to the launch of the firm&#8217;s upcoming iPhone 12.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p7\">Despite the lack of guidance, Yahoo Finance says that Bloomberg&#8217;s research shows that analysts expect the following results:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote8\"><p>\n  Revenue: $52.2 billion expected versus $53.8 billion in Q3&#160;2019.</p>\n<p>  Earnings per share: $2.06 expected versus $2.18 in Q3&#160;2019.\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2 id=\"graphical-visualization\">Graphical Visualization</h2>\n<p id=\"p9\">After the break, we&#8217;ve compiled a graphical visualization of 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Apple Music for Web Debuts New Beta Version with Fresh Design and ‘Listen Now’","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=64049","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/4ec99907-d17b-4329-899e-ae65ca6170eb.jpeg\" alt=\"The new Apple Music web beta.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">The new Apple Music web beta.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">It&#8217;s been less than a year since Apple launched <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/news/apple-launches-web-based-music-app-as-public-beta/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">its first public beta of the Apple Music web player</a>, which after several months came out of beta earlier this year and resides at <a href=\"https://music.apple.com\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">music.apple.com</a>. On the heels of an updated Music app in this fall&#8217;s releases of iOS, iPadOS, macOS, and more, the company isn&#8217;t delaying keeping its web player in-sync with the app versions. A new public beta of Apple Music for web can be accessed now at <a href=\"https://beta.music.apple.com\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">beta.music.apple.com</a>, sporting a design to match the changes seen in the forthcoming macOS 11 and iPadOS 14, and a new Listen Now page that replaces the prior For You option.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">The design refresh doesn&#8217;t bring major changes, just aesthetic tweaks to elements like the sidebar. Listen Now represents the most substantial update, but it still works similarly to the former For You page. It contains collections of recommended albums and playlists based on your listening activity, alongside Apple Music&#8217;s algorithmic playlists like New Music Mix and Chill Mix. You&#8217;ll also find Recently Played, New Releases from artists in your Library, and a new prominent section called Top Picks. After using Listen Now in the OS betas for the last couple months, I&#8217;ve grown to prefer it over For You, despite there being relatively few differences between the two. Having Top Picks front and center, for example, is a better choice for me than For You&#8217;s placement of the algorithmic playlists up top, since I rarely listen to those.</p>\n<p id=\"p4\">It&#8217;s great to see that Apple Music&#8217;s web player will be updated on the same cycle as its apps. Apple&#8217;s history with iterating its web apps isn&#8217;t great (iCloud.com, anyone?), but to better compete against Spotify, which has a first-class web player, a more intentional approach for Apple Music is needed.</p>\n<p id=\"p5\">Anyone can access the beta version of Apple Music&#8217;s web player at <a href=\"https://beta.music.apple.com\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">beta.music.apple.com</a>, while the previous version is still accessible at <a href=\"https://music.apple.com\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">music.apple.com</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Schiller will retain oversight of the App Store and Apple Events, and continue reporting directly to CEO Tim Cook, but most of his current responsibilities will shift to Greg (Joz) Joswiak, who takes over the title of senior vice president of Worldwide Marketing.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">Here&#8217;s Schiller on this significant day of transition:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote4\"><p>\n  &#8220;It has been a dream come true for me to work at Apple, on so many products I love, with all of these great friends &#8212; Steve, Tim, and so many more,&#8221; said Schiller. &#8220;I first started at Apple when I was 27, this year I turned 60 and it is time for some planned changes in my life. I&#8217;ll keep working here as long as they will have me, I bleed six colors, but I also want to make some time in the years ahead for my family, friends, and a few personal projects I care deeply about.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p5\">Tim Cook remarks:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote6\"><p>\n  &#8220;Phil has helped make Apple the company it is today and his contributions are broad, vast, and run deep. In this new role he will continue to provide the incredible thought partnership, and guidance that have defined his decades at Apple&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p7\">Schiller has been one of the most visible members of Apple&#8217;s team for a long time, most notably owning primary responsibility for introducing new hardware at Apple keynotes, such as the latest iPhone models each year. His expected absence from future such occasions will mark a stark shift for the company.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/B23B1602-D05B-4744-BE8A-D50AA1B8A904-1596561809760.jpeg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p9\">Joswiak, who takes Schiller&#8217;s former role, is no unfamiliar face himself. He has over two decades of leadership experience within Apple, and in recent years has become a regular presence at Apple events as well. Despite being a major force within the company, however, Joswiak&#8217;s presence on the executive team represents a new level of leadership for him, and come with major new responsibilities.</p>\n<p id=\"p10\">After many years of stability at the highest levels of leadership, time is finally catching up with Apple&#8217;s executive team. Chief Design Officer Jony Ive <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/news/jony-ive-to-leave-apple-to-form-new-design-firm-and-sabih-kahn-named-svp-of-operations/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">departed the company</a> last summer, just a few months after Angela Ahrendts <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/linked/apple-retail-chief-angela-ahrendts-leaving-company-replaced-by-deirdre-obrien/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">vacated her role as SVP of Retail</a>. While today&#8217;s news follows a different pattern, since Schiller is remaining with the company despite his reduced role, so much change at the top of the organization feels very new for the modern Apple era.</p>\n<p id=\"p11\">As someone who began following Apple closely only about a decade ago, not long before the passing of former presentation chief Steve Jobs, I&#8217;ve seen a lot of Schiller product introductions and am really going to miss his presence for many keynotes to come.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Many restaurants have been unable to offer indoor dining, and the lack of a commute as much of society adjusted to work-from-home life provided the opportunity to spend more time in the kitchen. Bread baking became <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/04/09/health/bread-baking-health-benefits-coronavirus-wellness/index.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a popular habit</a>, but so did home cooking in general. All of this has brought an influx of new entrants to cooking.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">I&#8217;m not new to cooking, but I&#8217;ve nonetheless found myself in the market for a better solution for recipe management, meal planning, and cooking walkthroughs. The app I&#8217;ve found best suited for my needs is <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/crouton-cooking-companion/id1461650987?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Crouton</a>, from developer Devin Davies.</p>\n<p id=\"p4\">Crouton offers a handful of valuable aids for cooking, but the feature at the center of it all is the app&#8217;s recipe management system. Once you have recipes stored in the app, you can view those recipes in a well-designed, intuitive format, but you&#8217;ll also be able to easily assign recipes to your weekly meal plan, add ingredients to your grocery list, or be guided through step-by-step instructions while cooking.</p>\n<p id=\"p5\"><!--more--></p>\n<p id=\"p6\">To get started adding recipes, there are a few options available: you can create new recipes via manual entry, import recipes from <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/paprika-recipe-manager-3/id1303222868?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Paprika</a>, or import recipes from the web. I used the Paprika importer my first day with the app and it saved me a lot of time. Since then, my primary method of adding recipes has been via web imports. While there&#8217;s unfortunately no share extension or action extension to do this directly from Safari, Crouton&#8217;s web importer is nearly as pain-free an experience. Copy the URL for a recipe you found online to the clipboard, then open Crouton and you&#8217;ll see a pop-up offering to import that recipe into your collection. You can modify any details you&#8217;d like, but in my experience the web importer has done a solid job on every try.</p>\n<p id=\"p7\">Recipes can be sorted into folders you create, otherwise they all live in the default &#8216;All Recipes&#8217; folder. One nice touch is that recipes can be stored in multiple folders at once, making it more like a tagging system than a traditional folder approach. It&#8217;s an important detail since plenty of recipes don&#8217;t fit neatly into a single category.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/738c6ca4-b066-4f94-97ba-217831b75c3a.png\" alt=\"Crouton on iPad features a two-panel layout.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Crouton on iPad features a two-panel layout.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p9\">My two favorite aspects of Crouton are its intuitive modern design for parsing recipes and the ease of adding those recipes to a meal plan.</p>\n<p id=\"p10\">On a recipe&#8217;s detail screen, everything is neatly organized in a layout that makes sense. Rounded rectangles are used to house each of the different blocks of data available for recipes, such as prep and cook times, the ingredients list, and numbered step-by-step cooking directions. As someone who considers himself barely more than a cooking novice, Crouton&#8217;s playful aesthetics help make recipes feel more approachable to me.</p>\n<p id=\"p11\">Another thing I appreciate about the recipe detail screen is that it&#8217;s not over-cluttered with features you may not care about; rather, every feature has been thoughtfully added and fits well into the layout of the page. Those features include the ability to scale a recipe&#8217;s ingredients for the number of people you&#8217;re feeding, hit the play button to enter cooking mode and get one instructional step on-screen at a time, tap the shopping cart item to easily add select ingredients to your grocery list, and share the recipe in a variety of formats &#8211; the PDF option even lets you customize the document&#8217;s design and contents.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/fb039a5f-45a8-4d05-9b9d-ad6bbbc3197f.png\" alt=\"Cooking mode is great on the iPad, where ingredients are visible on the left and instructions on the right.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Cooking mode is great on the iPad, where ingredients are visible on the left and instructions on the right.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p13\">Speaking of cooking mode, the most natural way to cycle through each instructional step is to swipe through them, or use the arrow buttons at the bottom of the screen. But it&#8217;s worth noting that there&#8217;s a hands-free mode too on devices featuring the TrueDepth camera system. Developer Devin Davies has implemented a clever way of using the TrueDepth camera&#8217;s face detection features such that you can wink at your device to have it cycle through cooking steps. A right wink moves to the next step and a left wink moves backwards. So if you can set your compatible iPhone or iPad Pro at a level where it can see your face well, this is a convenient way to keep dirty hands away from your device. You can enable this feature via the eye icon in the top-right corner of cooking mode.</p>\n<p id=\"p14\">Meal planning has a dedicated tab in Crouton&#8217;s tab bar, and consists of a simple list of current and upcoming days in descending order. Tap a day and you&#8217;ll see your collection of recipes, sorted into their appropriate folders, for you to choose from. You can add either a single recipe to a day, or multiple recipes to cover not only the main entree but also any sides and/or dessert you plan to prepare. There&#8217;s nothing innovative about the way any of this works, but there doesn&#8217;t need to be &#8211; its simplicity is its strength.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/b6b9430d-bcb8-45a0-b0cb-402b6dcd33bb.png\" alt=\"Recipe folders (left) and the meal planner with a web recipe import pop-up (right).\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Recipe folders (left) and the meal planner with a web recipe import pop-up (right).</p></div>\n<p id=\"p16\">I don&#8217;t use the grocery function of Crouton, but it&#8217;s worth noting that it&#8217;s very easy to add ingredients from your recipes to the in-app Groceries tab, which can also hold grocery items you manually add. The best part is that this tab can be synced with Reminders, so that the contents of your grocery list in reminders is reflected in Crouton as well, and vice versa.</p>\n<p id=\"p17\">Finally, Crouton comes equipped with the sort of system features you would expect from a modern app. Dark mode support enables automatic theme switching, context menus are used throughout the UI, and you can choose from a selection of alternate app icons for your Home screen. Near and dear to my heart, there&#8217;s an iPad client that supports Split View and Slide Over multitasking, and the app also takes good advantage of the larger display with a two-panel layout. I&#8217;ve found the iPad app especially useful while in the process of cooking, since I can sit the device in Magic Keyboard atop our kitchen island and swipe through cooking directions one page at a time.</p>\n<hr id=\"hr18\"><p id=\"p19\">Crouton makes meal planning easy, provides a beautiful way to store and view your recipes, and plays a key role in the cooking process. I&#8217;m not someone who cooks more than once or twice a week, so it&#8217;s possible that for someone more active in the kitchen there are advanced features missing that I&#8217;m unaware of, but I&#8217;ve found that Crouton offers exactly what I need in this type of app. It&#8217;s modern, keeps things simple in a good way, and offers valuable utility with style.</p>\n<p id=\"p20\">Crouton is a <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/crouton-cooking-companion/id1461650987?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">free download on the App Store</a>, with a one-time In-App Purchase available to remove recipe storage limits.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Apple releases a new environmental report showing the company&#8217;s progress in environmental efforts, and alongside the release of <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/environment/pdf/Apple_Environmental_Progress_Report_2020.pdf\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">this year&#8217;s report</a>, the company has <a decade ahead</a>:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote2\"><p>\n  Apple today unveiled its plan to become carbon neutral across its entire business, manufacturing supply chain, and product life cycle by Climate action can be the foundation for a new era of innovative potential, job creation, and durable economic growth. With our commitment to carbon neutrality, we hope to be a ripple in the pond that creates a much larger change.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p3\">Achieving carbon neutrality for its corporate operations was a nice milestone for the company, but this new commitment appears far more challenging. Apple works with third-party suppliers and manufacturers all around the world to build its devices, and fulfilling this new goal depends a lot on those third parties. It will be interesting to see over the next decade all of the different actions that will be taken to find success in carbon neutrality, but the report of Apple <a href=\"https://www.macrumors.com/2020/06/28/kuo-no-charger-in-iphone-12-box/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">including fewer accessories in the box with new iPhone purchases</a> certainly seems like it would help.</p>\n<p>→ Source: <a href='https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2020/07/apple-commits-to-be-100-percent-carbon-neutral-for-its-supply-chain-and-products-by-2030/' target='_blank'>apple.com</a></p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 21 Jul 2020 14:48:14 +0000","feedId":526,"bgimg":"https://56243e3f6f46fe44a301-deabeb5f3878e3553d0b065ea974f9bf.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/256px.png","linkMd5":"f069b217b323b81a76eb0b8743ce4437","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn89@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-54-46-345_901ee973c59d45b7.webp","metaImg":"https://56243e3f6f46fe44a301-deabeb5f3878e3553d0b065ea974f9bf.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/256px.png","destWidth":256,"destHeight":256,"author":"Ryan Christoffel"},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"Due for Mac Modernized with New Design and Features","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63948","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%400-1595785955853.5x.png\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">A full-fledged task manager is terrific for many projects, but if you dump your entire life into one, it can quickly become a cluttered mess. At the same time, if you&#8217;re focused on a big project, it&#8217;s easy to let everything that&#8217;s not in your task manager slip through the cracks. One strategy for attacking the problem that has worked well for me is using a separate, lightweight app for tasks like remembering to take out the garbage, pick up medicine at the pharmacy, or publish an article when an embargo lifts.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">In the past, I&#8217;ve used <a href=\"https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/id390017969\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Due on the iPhone and iPad</a> for these sorts of tasks. There has been a Mac version of Due for years too, but it hadn&#8217;t been updated in about two years and was showing its age. However, with today&#8217;s update, <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/due-reminders-countdown-timers/id524373870\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Due for Mac</a> joins the iOS version with a fully-modern design and slate of new features, putting it on par with the outstanding iOS version, which <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/reviews/due-adds-modern-shortcuts-support-with-new-reminder-creation-parameters/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">I&#8217;ve covered</a> <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/reviews/due-30-adds-pure-black-theme-custom-snooze-times-and-haptic-feedback/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">in the past</a>.</p>\n<p id=\"p4\"><!--more--></p>\n<p id=\"p5\">If you&#8217;re not familiar with Due, the app&#8217;s strength is the ability to create reminders and timers quickly. Reminders can be one-off or repeating events and can be entered using natural language syntax that auto-populates the due date and time field. According to the developer, Due&#8217;s natural language engine has been improved with today&#8217;s version 20.1.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Screenshot%202020-07-28%2007-1595941291032.59.43.png\" alt=\"Due detects dates and times and gives you options for how to treat them.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Due detects dates and times and gives you options for how to treat them.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p7\">My favorite touch here is that when as you type a due date or time into a new reminder, Due provides keyboard shortcuts to set the date and time and then remove the date text you typed, set the date but leave the text in the reminder, or ignore the typed date text altogether. I use these options to do things like set reminders that contain a deadline in the description but will go off in advance of the deadline. For example, I can set a reminder to &#8216;Publish article at 10 am&#8217; ignoring &#8216;10 am&#8217; and then typing &#8216;9:45 am&#8217; and using that as the time for an alert.</p>\n<p id=\"p8\">Another of Due&#8217;s hallmarks is the ability to auto-snooze reminders and timers. For important tasks that need to be completed on a schedule, auto-snooze is terrific because it will remind you at regular intervals that an item is due or a timer finished running until you shut it off. Rescheduling a reminder is simple, too, using keyboard shortcuts, the right-click menu, or menu item to delay it 10 minutes, 1 hour, or 1 day.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%202%400-1595787137788.5x.png\" alt=\"The difference in design between Due before (left) and after (right) its update is striking.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">The difference in design between Due before (left) and after (right) its update is striking.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p10\">The difference between the old version of Due and version 20.1 is apparent immediately upon opening the app for the first time. Due has dispensed with the top and bottom window chrome. Instead of a toolbar at the top of the window, there&#8217;s a narrow sidebar for navigating the app&#8217;s sections and creating new reminders or timers. A search field also spans the top of the window, which is a terrific addition for quickly locating a reminder or timer if you&#8217;ve got an extensive collection of either.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Untitled%202%400-1595786685919.5x.png\" alt=\"Reminders are organized into four temporal categories that are collapsible.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Reminders are organized into four temporal categories that are collapsible.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p12\">Reminders are now organized automatically by due date into four categories: Today, Tomorrow, Next 7 Days, and Future. Each category can be collapsed with the disclosure triangle next to its heading, allowing you to focus on one section at a time, which is another nice touch for those with long lists of reminders. Readability is also enhanced by the ability to adjust text size in the app&#8217;s Preferences.</p>\n<p id=\"p13\">Due&#8217;s redesign extends to its use of typography and color too. Each reminder category features big, bold titles that break up your list of reminders into meaningful sections. The default theme is Vanilla Lilac and features a light purple sidebar and section text against a light window background. The app includes another light and two dark themes, all of which I like a lot: Lavender, Slate Dark, and Pure Black. There&#8217;s also an option to switch themes based on your Mac&#8217;s light/dark mode settings that lets you pick whatever combination of light and dark themes you prefer.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Screenshot%202020-07-26%2008-1595788561970.08.45.png\" alt=\"Due is highly customizable.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Due is highly customizable.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p15\">The redesign of Due is a significant leap forward and an excellent illustration of the importance of design. Mac app design had long since passed by the previous version of Due. With version 20.1, Due not only feels at home among other modern Mac apps, but it&#8217;s easier to navigate and visually superior to the previous version&#8217;s approach.</p>\n<p id=\"p16\">Due&#8217;s update on the Mac runs deeper than just its new design, though. There are new features too. Due can be run exclusively from the menu bar if you prefer that to seeing its icon in your dock. I try to limit the number of apps in my menu bar, so it&#8217;s not a feature that I&#8217;ll use, but it&#8217;s a nice option to have. Instead, I run Due as a standard dock-based app that launches on login and use a custom global keyboard shortcut to quickly bring the app to the foreground.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/Screenshot%202020-07-26%2013-1595788347371.14.15%400.5x.png\" alt=\"Like the iOS version, Due for Mac supports gestures.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Like the iOS version, Due for Mac supports gestures.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p18\">The app has also added gesture support, allowing users to swipe left on a trackpad with two fingers to mark a reminder as complete and swipe further to delete it. The same gesture is used in timers to reset a countdown or delete a timer. Bulk editing is available now too. Simply highlight several reminders at once to mark them all as complete, reschedule or delete them, or change their alert and auto-snooze settings.</p>\n<p id=\"p19\">Due for the Mac has adopted the same sort of business model as its iOS and iPadOS counterpart. The Mac app is a separate $14.99 purchase from the iOS and iPadOS version and comes with one free year of updates from the date of purchase. After that, for an additional $9.99/year, you can purchase the app&#8217;s Upgrade Pass to receive upgrades for an additional year. If you stop subscribing, any feature updates you get through the subscription will remain available.</p>\n<p id=\"p20\">When I&#8217;m in the midst of a big project, I have a tendency to let other things slide more than I should. I&#8217;ve tried throwing those items into OmniFocus or another task manager I&#8217;m using at the time, but it only makes things worse. Although a task manager ensures that those items won&#8217;t get lost entirely, they have a tendency to clutter my task manager and thus add to a sense of being overwhelmed.</p>\n<p id=\"p21\">It&#8217;s times like this when I turn to Due. Many of the things I drop into the app are one-off reminders. Others are the kind of repeating tasks that are all too easy to forget about if I&#8217;m deep into writing or some other task. However, I also turn to Due for things that absolutely need to be done by a specific time. I use this sparingly, but auto-snooze is a fantastic way to ensure something gets done when it needs to be, especially since it syncs over iCloud so my reminders follow me wherever I happen to be. If you&#8217;ve ever needed a little extra prodding to get something done on time, Due is an excellent solution.</p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac. Plus, it&#8217;s made in Italy.</p>\n</p><a href='https://club.macstories.net/?utm_source=ms&#038;utm_medium=rss'>Join Now</a>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 14 Aug 2020 16:16:47 +0000","feedId":526,"bgimg":"https://56243e3f6f46fe44a301-deabeb5f3878e3553d0b065ea974f9bf.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/256px.png","linkMd5":"c7c0996e173900022755c91005a71d8a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn89@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-54-46-345_901ee973c59d45b7.webp","destWidth":256,"destHeight":256,"author":"John Voorhees","enclosureType":"audio/mpeg","enclosureUrl":"https://cdn.simplecast.com/audio/0de98b/0de98bba-5e4d-4879-94dc-8c76a3a88322/613a43e3-59b0-4de1-8e83-690b5b65e8a6/macstories-unwind-august-14-episode_tc.mp3","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-itunes-2x1495584446433.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn29@2020_6/2020/08/16/11-54-48-951_44f6e726042a0d5b.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-overcast-2x1495584446439.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_1/2020/08/16/11-54-46-435_63962739202511e1.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-pocket-casts-2x1495584446442.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn74@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-54-49-676_683cc37726177cc0.webp","https://31468fb5fb2bdd537aee-cb22f1c32609fa6d332a03da76e227e5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/button-rss-2x1495584446444.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn37@2020_5/2020/08/16/11-54-49-107_962140602f5518bd.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:54:40","title":"The Developer Debrief on WWDC 2020","link":"https://www.macstories.net/?p=63902","description":"<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/8f544ce0-60ab-4edf-a2ce-3f8eece79b6e.jpeg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p2\">Weeks removed from Apple wrapping up its first all-virtual WWDC, many of us are still digesting what the <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/tag/wwdc-2020/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">conference&#8217;s announcements</a> mean for the future of our favorite products.</p>\n<p id=\"p3\">Federico, John, and I have all shared various takeaways from the conference, and I&#8217;m sure we&#8217;ll have a lot more to report as we continue using the betas this summer and review Apple&#8217;s OS updates this fall. But our perspective is limited to our profession as journalists, so we also wanted to hear from the people this conference was really built for: developers.</p>\n<p id=\"p4\">WWDC has grown into an exciting conference for Apple users all around the globe, but its core identity is still ultimately an event for app developers. As a result, I wanted to speak with a variety of developers to get their reactions to the conference. These included:</p>\n<ul id=\"ul5\"><li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/bhansmeyer?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Becky Hansmeyer</a>, creator of <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/snapthread-video-editor/id1277445843?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Snapthread</a> and <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/yarnbuddy-knit-and-crochet/id1267678125?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">YarnBuddy</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/_chuckyc?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Charlie Chapman</a>, creator of <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/dark-noise/id1465439395?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Dark Noise</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/_DavidSmith?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">David Smith</a>, creator of <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/watchsmith/id1483088503?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Watchsmith</a>, <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/sleep/id1038440371?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Sleep++</a>, and <a href=\"https://david-smith.org/apps/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">many more apps</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/jamesthomson?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">James Thomson</a>, creator of <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/pcalc/id284666222?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">PCalc</a> and <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/dice-by-pcalc/id1468680083?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Dice</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/kthomas901?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Kaya Thomas</a>, creator of <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/we-read-too/id908782619?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">We Read Too</a> and Sr. iOS Engineer at <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/calm/id571800810?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Calm</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/simonbs?s=21\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Simon St&#248;vring</a>, creator of <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/scriptable/id1405459188?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Scriptable</a>, <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/data-jar/id1453273600?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Data Jar</a>, and <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/jayson/id1447750768?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Jayson</a></li>\n</ul><p id=\"p6\">My sincere thanks to these developers for taking the time to share their thoughts, and for their years of valuable contributions toward making Apple&#8217;s app ecosystem as strong and robust as it is today.</p>\n<p id=\"p7\">Interview questions for each developer ranged from the things that most excited them at the conference to surprises and disappointments, their read on how in-touch Apple is with the developer community, the current evolution of software development, and each developer was also generous enough to share a sneak peek at new technologies they&#8217;re working to implement in their apps.</p>\n<aside class=\"aside aligncenter aside-narrow\" id=\"aside8\"><h3 class=\"pre-title\" id=\"supported-by\">Supported By</h3>\n<h2 id=\"concepts\">Concepts</h2>\n\n<p></p><center><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/icon-1595254554207.png\" alt=\"\"></center>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://concepts.app/download?utm_source=macstories)\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer noopener noreferrer\">Concepts</a></strong>: Sketch, Note, Draw</p>\n</aside><p id=\"p9\"><!--more--></p>\n<h2 id=\"excitement-disappointment-and-surprise\">Excitement, Disappointment, and Surprise</h2>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/2b5bb39f-b1cd-46c5-8154-63e5e77885aa.jpeg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p11\">When I asked about the biggest positive takeaways from WWDC, most developers focused on the conference itself. David Smith summarizes their feedback well:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote12\"><p>\n  &#8220;The experience was without a doubt one of my favorite yet.&#160; The clarity and personality of the pre-recorded videos was excellent.&#160; The Labs experience was just as useful as during in-person events.&#160; Even the sense of community felt way better than I would have predicted.&#160; I really liked this format and hope that Apple incorporates most of it in future years.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p13\">In terms of specific announcements, a highlight for Kaya Thomas was App Clips, the new technology that enables small pieces of app data to be accessed on-demand without installing a whole app. Thomas said of the feature:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote14\"><p>\n  &#8220;It&#8217;s something I would have never guessed was coming and is a really innovative new experience for helping with discovery of apps. It&#8217;s not a use case that works for every app, but for the apps it does, it will allow developers to worry less about the drop-off rate that comes with the user having to go to the App Store to download your app.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/975996a1-b528-4242-9020-05648c2fb27e.jpeg\" alt=\"App Clips are a new way for users to discover apps.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">App Clips are a new way for users to discover apps.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p16\">Many developers were enthused and surprised by all of the Mac-related news from the conference.</p>\n<p id=\"p17\">Charlie Chapman:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote18\"><p>\n  &#8220;Between all the Catalyst improvements, SwiftUI, and iPhone apps coming straight to the Mac with Apple Silicon, it feels like the Mac is being opened up as a platform for iOS developers, and that&#8217;s really exciting. Seeing the Mac get so much love and attention this year was definitely a highlight, and I think we&#8217;re about to see a lot more activity in Mac software than we&#8217;ve seen in a while.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p19\">Becky Hansmeyer:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote20\"><p>\n  &#8220;I was most surprised by the macOS redesign. I was so focused on the transition to Apple Silicon that it never occurred to me they would drastically change the look of the OS this year. I was also pretty surprised by the automatic availability of iOS apps on the Mac.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p21\">James Thomson:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote22\"><p>\n  &#8220;Catalyst got very welcome changes this year, and even a shout out in the keynote. It looks like almost everything I was asking for a year ago has now been added, which is great. And the fact that Apple was using it for Messages, one of their most important apps, gives me confidence I can rely on it sticking around.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/78ee86e2-ab0c-4452-a4d8-6be17e9a937e.jpeg\" alt=\"WWDC brought a lot of exciting Mac changes.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">WWDC brought a lot of exciting Mac changes.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p24\">But there were also, of course, some disappointments. Again there was a lot of commonality among developers, with changes in widget functionality being a common concern. For example, Thomson confirmed he won&#8217;t be able to ship a new widget with the same feature set as his existing one:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote25\"><p>\n  &#8220;A lot of people love the existing PCalc widget, and I&#8217;m sad that it will eventually have to go away &#8211; maybe not this year, but probably next, [due to] the new widget architecture not allowing complex interactivity.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p26\">Simon St&#248;vring shared his hope that, with so much happening on the Mac, this would have been the year the platform gained Shortcuts:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote27\"><p>\n  &#8220;I felt confident that we would get Shortcuts on the Mac, and with everything else Apple announced this year, I think it would fit right in. We&#8217;ll certainly see more iOS and iPadOS apps coming to the Mac soon, if not because of the new additions to Catalyst and SwiftUI, then because these apps will be available when Macs with Apple Silicon are released &#8211; these iOS and iPadOS apps would come with shortcuts built in.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p28\">Kaya Thomas was let down by another year&#8217;s absence of a key developer tool:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote29\"><p>\n  &#8220;I was most disappointed that there was no announcement of any new continuous integration/delivery tooling. Since Apple acquired Buddybuild a few years ago, every year I&#8217;ve hoped there would be an announcement of what they&#8217;ve done with it. There are a lot of continuous integration/delivery services out there, but it would be incredible to have a complete native solution made for Apple platforms.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2 id=\"is-apple-listening\">Is Apple Listening?</h2>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/71b83ec0-65e2-496b-be9c-7243af6ba490.jpeg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p31\">Apple has a notorious penchant not only for secrecy, but also for doing all of its product work in seeming isolation from the outside world. Users and developers alike are often left wondering if the company truly listens to feedback or not, an issue exacerbated by the fact that it often takes years of behind-the-scenes work for Apple to address such feedback. We all love a good Apple surprise, but for developers in particular, whose livelihood is tied to the choices Apple makes, being left in the dark can be scary.</p>\n<p id=\"p32\">WWDC is usually the prime occasion for Apple to show the development community that it&#8217;s listening, as the company unveils new OS versions, frameworks, APIs, and other tools designed to empower making the best apps possible. Following the 2020 virtual conference I asked developers whether they felt heard by Apple this year. Unsurprisingly their answers varied, and in some cases depended on what those developers were hoping for.</p>\n<p id=\"p33\">Simon St&#248;vring, for example, was encouraged by the significant investment he sees from Apple into areas that are central to his apps:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote34\"><p>\n  &#8220;In the past few years I&#8217;ve been working quite a lot with the Intents and IntentsUI frameworks, Apple&#8217;s frameworks that let developers integrate with Siri shortcuts, and it is clear to me that in 2019 and 2020 those frameworks received major improvements to accommodate the needs of developers.</p>\n<p>  Examples include the support for input and output parameters that were added to Shortcuts in iOS 13, which was probably at the top of most Shortcuts users&#8217; and developers&#8217; wish list. Not only did Apple add support for parameters, but they also provided a very flexible solution.</p>\n<p>  Another example is the in-app intent handling that was added to iOS 14. This new API lets developers implement Shortcuts actions that are more powerful than previously, something I&#8217;ve heard several developers wish for since the introduction of Shortcuts in 2018.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p35\">The common tendency to judge Apple&#8217;s progress by its relevance to your own projects highlights the reality that no matter how large the company grows, it can&#8217;t build everything every year. Kaya Thomas echoed this idea:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote36\"><p>\n  &#8220;It&#8217;s never 100% disappointment or 100% wishes fulfilled. There were still some disappointments regarding things developers were looking forward to, for example Apple announcing a new CI tool as a follow-up to their acquisition of Buddybuild. On the other hand, the new StoreKit testing capabilities was a long-awaited ask that they finally fulfilled.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p37\">In terms of more general thoughts on how much Apple is listening, I found it interesting how commonality was found among those newer to the development community and those with longer histories working on Apple platforms. Everyone found Apple&#8217;s receptivity to developer feedback generally positive, but mentioned a few areas that can still lead to frustrations.</p>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/ddef53fe-891f-4f0d-8e2d-082b0af50b73.jpeg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p39\">Representing that newer wave of developers is Becky Hansmeyer and Charlie Chapman.</p>\n<p id=\"p40\">Hansmeyer:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote41\"><p>\n  &#8220;I feel like Apple is definitely making an effort to listen to developers more; however, it still feels like there are several layers of corporate policy and bureaucracy (and perhaps stubbornness?) that make addressing developers&#8217; concerns a very slow, frustrating process.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p42\">Chapman:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote43\"><p>\n  &#8220;I haven&#8217;t been an Apple developer for very long so I can&#8217;t say for sure, but based on stories of the past it does seems like Apple&#8217;s a little more receptive to feedback from the developer community than they may have been before.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p44\">Long-time developers James Thomson and David Smith see Apple&#8217;s attentiveness as largely the same as the past, but like Hansmeyer and Chapman, their views are generally balanced between optimism and realism.</p>\n<p id=\"p45\">Thomson:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote46\"><p>\n  &#8220;[Apple listens] a reasonable amount&#8230;pretty much the same as always. There is an element of &#8220;Apple knows best&#8221; to some of the changes, which you are expected to get on board with or be left behind, but that&#8217;s always been the case. In other areas though, there are definitely things where they have gone beyond what I even imagined they would.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p47\">Smith:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote48\"><p>\n  &#8220;I&#8217;d say that they are listening to developers about the same as always.&#160; They are responsive and helpful in the fine-grained aspects of development, making changes and accommodations to their APIs based on our needs.&#160;But they also don&#8217;t often let the vocal complaints of parts of their development community distract them from their internal vision for the platform.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2 id=\"the-unification-of-software-development\">The Unification of Software Development</h2>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/a9b5c3c5-7e78-4041-b933-67e586c51aef.jpeg\" alt=\"Build once, ship everywhere is a theme of modern Apple development.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Build once, ship everywhere is a theme of modern Apple development.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p50\">A common theme of the last two WWDCs has been Apple&#8217;s focus on helping developers more easily build cross-platform apps. In the modern Apple ecosystem, it&#8217;s rare to find an app that&#8217;s iPhone- or iPad-only, and there&#8217;s a shrinking number of Mac-only apps too. Apple may not be merging its software platforms, but it&#8217;s doing a lot to make them work seamlessly in tandem.</p>\n<p id=\"p51\">Becky Hansmeyer remarks:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote52\"><p>\n  &#8220;This year&#8217;s WWDC has made me feel incredibly excited and optimistic about the future of Apple platforms. It finally seems like Apple has a cohesive vision for its platform line-up and a clear understanding of each device&#8217;s particular strengths and roles in people&#8217;s everyday lives.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p53\">David Smith agrees:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote54\"><p>\n  &#8220;I feel very confident about the direction of Apple&#8217;s platforms right now.&#160; They have provided a cohesive vision for the future of their platforms from the Apple Watch to the Mac Pro.&#160; Many of the puzzle pieces that were required to make this happen have clearly been in the works for years and are now all falling into place.&#160;This foresight makes me feel good about the plans they have going forward and the thoughtfulness with which they are operating.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p55\">Simon St&#248;vring highlights a couple of those puzzle pieces as he echoes these comments:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote56\"><p>\n  &#8220;There are a lot of very exciting things going on right now. The unification, if not of the platforms then of the frameworks used by developers creating apps for the platforms, is very exciting. Now that we&#8217;re seeing the first year of iterations on SwiftUI and Catalyst, it&#8217;s becoming clear that they&#8217;ll play a big part in the future of Apple&#8217;s platforms. The opportunities for building fully native apps for all of Apple&#8217;s platforms is very encouraging.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2 id=\"summer-projects\">Summer Projects</h2>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/0544c7fd-505d-4c15-82a0-2fac5e92a8ad.jpeg\" alt=\"\"><p class=\"image-caption\"></p></div>\n<p id=\"p58\">As a big fan of the apps made by these developers, I couldn&#8217;t let them go without asking about the things they&#8217;ll be working on over the summer.</p>\n<p id=\"p59\">Kaya Thomas was one of many developers interested in building new widgets:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote60\"><p>\n  &#8220;I&#8217;m most excited about widgets, as a developer and consumer. Widgets being written in SwiftUI allows developers who can&#8217;t drop support for older OS versions to still be able to learn and use SwiftUI, which I strongly believe is the future of development for all Apple platforms. We aren&#8217;t limited by just having one widget and we can make them very configurable for our users. I think widgets will allow us to help save our users time by surfacing relevant and timely content right on their Home screens.</p>\n<p>  For We Read Too, I&#8217;m definitely exploring what a useful widget would look like, whether it&#8217;s showcasing the most recently added titles or a user&#8217;s recent favorited books.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p61\">James Thomson is using one of his apps to experiment with things he may want to implement in a different app:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote62\"><p>\n  &#8220;I am currently investigating the best way to build a next generation version of PCalc, and there are multiple paths I could take. Right now, I&#8217;m updating Dice by PCalc &#8211; which is really my small test app for new Apple technologies &#8211; to use the latest Catalyst features to make a more Mac-like experience. I&#8217;ll then see how I feel about using that for PCalc, or if I want to rewrite it all in SwiftUI.</p>\n<p>  If I had an Apple Silicon DTK machine, I couldn&#8217;t tell you anything because of the NDA. But I can say I&#8217;m pretty confident this processor transition will go smoothly for both developers and users, and it will be a lot easier to port existing apps to ARM than it was to go from PowerPC to Intel fifteen years ago.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p63\">Becky Hansmeyer just launched <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/yarnbuddy-knit-and-crochet/id1267678125?uo=4\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a new app</a>, but WWDC has given her plenty of additions to her to-do list:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote64\"><p>\n  &#8220;My latest iOS app, YarnBuddy, is written entirely in SwiftUI. I can&#8217;t wait to update it with a modern UI for the iPad, utilizing the new sidebar, toolbars, date/time pickers and color picker. I&#8217;m also planning to create some widgets, and possibly even bring the app to the Mac using Catalyst.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<div class=\"media-wrapper\"><img src=\"https://2672686a4cf38e8c2458-2712e00ea34e3076747650c92426bbb5.ssl.cf1.rackcdn.com/c43ad634-7f45-476a-b98a-990d65be1dc4.jpeg\" alt=\"Widgets are on a lot of developers&#8217; to-do lists.\"><p class=\"image-caption\">Widgets are on a lot of developers&#8217; to-do lists.</p></div>\n<p id=\"p66\">Charlie Chapman is at work on Dark Noise updates:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote67\"><p>\n  &#8220;Dark Noise will definitely get a few improvements thanks to new technology with iOS 14. The new widgets are way better than what I was offering before. In my testing so far, Siri integrations work much better than on iOS 13, and the &#8220;Maybe you wanted&#8230;&#8221; alternative responses were really easy to integrate with. The new Wind Down experience also feels like a pretty obvious fit for white noise apps like Dark Noise.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p68\">David Smith has several major areas of focus moving forward:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote69\"><p>\n  &#8220;This year has introduced three new opportunities that I&#8217;m hoping to immediately adopt.&#160;The first is adding iOS widgets to all my apps wherever I can.&#160;Being given access to a user&#8217;s Home screen provides for a whole new level of connection to my users.&#160;I&#8217;m very excited to see where that goes.&#160;</p>\n<p>  Secondly, I&#8217;m really excited by SwiftUI complications on the Apple Watch.&#160; I can enhance my current suite of complications with dramatically better performance and ability.&#160;</p>\n<p>  Lastly, I&#8217;m for the first time interested in trying my hand at making a Mac app.&#160;The toolset previously was just too high of a wall to scale, but this year enough of the pieces have come together that it feels like something I could tackle with some confidence.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<p id=\"p70\">Finally, Simon St&#248;vring rounds out the list with a very ambitious project slate too:</p>\n<blockquote id=\"blockquote71\"><p>\n  &#8220;I&#8217;ve got a handful of things I&#8217;d like to do with my apps over the summer. WidgetKit is an interesting opportunity for Scriptable. I&#8217;m working on a feature that lets users create a script that presents a widget. The script will automatically run periodically on the Home screen to present up to date information. This immediately fulfills a need I have during the summer, as I&#8217;ve created a widget using Scriptable that shows me the pollen count of the day. As a person that has hay fever, that is very handy.</p>\n<p>  The new in-app intent handling is amazing for Scriptable, making it possible to use file bookmarks in a shortcut, process larger images in a shortcut, and generally perform operations that are more memory-heavy in shortcuts. I&#8217;m sure this is going to be a big deal for many Shortcuts utilities out there.</p>\n<p>  The new additions to Catalyst are going to be great for Jayson on the Mac, in particular. I&#8217;m looking forward to replacing Jayson&#8217;s custom implementation of tabs with the native tabbed windows on the Mac.</p>\n<p>  I&#8217;m also very curious to try out the new support for keyboard navigation in both table views and collection views, something I&#8217;ve already implemented myself in Jayson, but if Apple&#8217;s implementation works, I&#8217;m more than happy to replace it with my implementation.</p>\n<p>  Data Jar might also benefit from the new in-app intent handling. I will most likely also see how it can benefit from some of the new system and more modern UI components.</p>\n<p>  I&#8217;m also working on a new app in which I&#8217;ve already adopted the three-column split view. Support for three-column split views was on my WWDC wishlist, so I&#8217;m very pleased Apple has added it this year. I can&#8217;t wait for more iPad apps to adopt this.&#8221;\n</p></blockquote>\n<hr id=\"hr72\"><p id=\"p73\">As I reflect on the takeaways from this group of developers, I think 2020 brought not only the most unique WWDC in recent years, but also one of the most important for Apple development. Fueled by the transition to Apple Silicon and a major UI redesign in Big Sur, Apple&#8217;s vision for the future of the Mac &#8211;&#160;the only platform where developers can currently build Apple apps &#8211; is clearer and more exciting than it has been in years. And with evolving tools like SwiftUI and Mac Catalyst, and new cross-platform OS features like redesigned widgets, it appears that Apple is on the cusp of doing something that&#8217;s been a challenge for the company for some time: moving its platforms forward in lock-step, with no platform neglected due to a scarcity of internal resources.</p>\n<p id=\"p74\">Besides surpassing my expectations for what a virtual conference could be, WWDC 2020 also made me optimistic that every Apple platform has a bright, exciting future ahead. That&#8217;s a great thing not only for developers, but also for every Apple user.</p>\n<hr id=\"hr75\"><p id=\"p76\"><em>You can also follow our 2020 Summer OS Preview Series through our <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/tag/os-preview-2020/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">dedicated hub</a>, or <a href=\"https://www.macstories.net/tag/os-preview-2020/feed/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">subscribe to its RSS feed</a>.</em></p>\n<hr /><h3>Support MacStories Directly</h3><p><p>Club MacStories offers exclusive access to <strong>extra MacStories content</strong>, delivered every week;  it&#8217;s also a way to support us directly.</p>\n<p>Club MacStories will help you discover the best apps for your devices and get the most out of your iPhone, iPad, and Mac.
